backing a new cryptocurrency and has landed at least $6 billion in gold reserves for the venture, <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2021-04-13/nyc-real-estate-mogul-secures-6-billion-in-gold-to-back-new-cryptocurrency\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">according to a Bloomberg report</a>. </p><p>Digital token DIGau&#39;s value will be pegged to gold&#39;s market price, guaranteed by liens against mining claims in Nevada and Arizona that were secured by Swig and his partner Stephen Braverman&#39;s company, Dignity Gold.</p><p>Swig, 60, said he searched worldwide for gold assets for 18 months to secure the $6 billion of reserves.</p><p>&#34;We&#39;re not reinventing the wheel here. What we&#39;re doing is applying the world&#39;s stable backing of a lot of things to a very advanced technology,&#34; Swig told Bloomberg in an interview published Tuesday. </p><p>Swig, who owns realty firm Brown Harris Stevens, said his interest in cryptocurrencies was piqued after his teenage son talked to him about the concept. Swig said DIGau will stand out as a gold-backed, U.S.-based crypto security that pays a dividend to token holders.</p><p>There&#39;s been a <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/news/bitcoin-btc-institutional-interest-cryptocurrencies-wall-street-tesla-microstrategy-jpmorgan-2021-3-1030194067\">jump in institutional interest in cryptocurrencies</a> including at investment bank Morgan Stanley and electric vehicle maker Tesla. Wall Street on Wednesday is greeting <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/coin-stock\">Coinbase</a>, the first <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-coinbase-ceo-brian-armstrong-landed-a-100-million-term-sheet-2021-4\">cryptocurrency exchange to begin trading publicly</a>. </p><p><em><strong>Read id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Instagram is now testing the option to allow users to decide if they want to see or hide &#34;likes.&#34; </p><p>Some users prefer not seeing the like count due to decreased social media pressure, while others want to see what&#39;s been a hit on the app, according to feedback from Instagram&#39;s previous tests. Now, the social media platform is using these differences in viewpoints to test the option for users to decide whether they want to see or remove the like tally. If the user opts for the latter, they&#39;ll be able to either hide all like counts across the platform, or hide likes on their own posts. </p><p>The social media giant first began exploring the removal of likes in 2019 via a test on users across seven countries,  <a href=\"https://twitter.com/instagram/status/1151605657642029056\">including</a> Canada, Australia, and Japan. According to a spokesperson at Facebook, Instagram&#39;s parent company, this was done to see whether the hiding of likes could &#34;lessen some pressure when posting&#34; to the app.</p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/instagram-tests-removing-public-like-counts-influencer-reactions-2021-3\">Instagram is testing removing public &#39;like&#39; counts and influencers say it would be good for the industry. Here&#39;s why.</a></em></p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/instagram-removing-likes-worldwide-test-2019-11\">Instagram saw &#34;positive feedback&#34;</a> during this testing stage, although the concept also received some <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/instagram-tests-taking-away-likes-celebrities-influencers-reactions-kim-kardashian-2019-11#minaj-went-on-to-speculate-that-instagram-was-hiding-likes-to-manipulate-what-posts-users-saw-in-their-feed-regardless-of-how-much-engagement-posts-were-getting-2\">backlash from celebrities and influencers</a>. </p><p>&#34;We&#39;re testing this because we want Instagram to be a place where people feel comfortable expressing themselves,&#34; a Facebook spokesperson told Insider in 2019. &#34;This includes helping people to focus on the photos and videos they share, not how many likes they get.&#34;</p><p>In March, Instagram <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/instagram-removing-likes-what-it-will-look-like-2019-11\">again removed the like count</a> for some users. But this time, it was an accident caused by a bug. </p><p>The removal of likes and reactions is also being tested on Facebook, according to the spokesperson. Like Instagram, Facebook <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/facebook-hiding-like-count-test-rollout-australia-this-week-instagram-2019-9\">began testing this </a>in 2019.</p><div 02:15:08","updatedTime":"2021-04-15 02:15:08","title":"What China can learn about using its 'mini-carrier strike groups' from watching US Navy operations","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/china-can-learn-about-navy-deployments-by-watching-us-navy-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6076f379420615001817562f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Navy aircraft carrier Theodore Roosevelt\" height=\"1000\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>US Navy aircraft carrier USS Theodore Roosevelt in the South China Sea, April 9, 2021.\n<p class=\"copyright\">US Navy/MCS Seaman Nadia Lund</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>A combination of vessel types has military observers speculating about how China can better deploy ships and aircraft.</li>\n<li>Beijing has launched just two of its six planned aircraft carrier strike groups, but other ships could help fill the gap.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>As the world&#39;s two biggest naval fleets <a href=\"https://www.scmp.com/news/china/diplomacy/article/3129036/us-china-relations-military-tensions-continue-rise-over-taiwan\" data-v-2a60e86e=\"\">engage in the Indo-Pacific region</a>, China&#39;s People&#39;s Liberation Army can observe and learn from the United States Navy in adapting future tactical combined operations, according to defence analysts.</p><p>They said the operators of China&#39;s Type 075 amphibious assault vessels could examine the US deployment of an amphibious-ready group (ARG) to the <a href=\"https://www.scmp.com/topics/south-china-sea\" data-v-2a60e86e=\"\">South China Sea</a>, which was led by <a href=\"https://www.scmp.com/news/china/diplomacy/article/3128808/south-china-sea-us-bolsters-presence-amphibious-assault-ship\" data-v-2a60e86e=\"\">the USS Makin Island landing helicopter dock (LHD)</a> and joined the USS Theodore Roosevelt Carrier Strike Group on April 9 for exercises.</p><p>The USS Makin Island is a 40,000-tonne Wasp-class amphibious assault ship able to carry a detachment of Marine F-35B Lightning II Joint Strike Fighters. The LHD and two San Antonio-class landing platform dock (LPD) amphibious transport ships - the USS Somerset and USS San Diego - as well as several helicopter and assault craft units form the Makin Island ARG.</p><p>&#34;The displacement size and functions of the Wasp-class LHD are similar to the PLA&#39;s Type 075 LHD, while the San Antonio-class transport docks are similar to China&#39;s Type 071 landing platform docks (LPD),&#34; Hong Kong-based military commentator Song Zhongping said.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6076f466420615001817563b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Navy amphibious transport dock USS Somerset\" height=\"1333\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>US Navy amphibious transport dock ship USS Somerset in the Bay of Bengal, April 7, 2021.\n<p class=\"copyright\">US Marine Corps/Lance Cpl. Brendan Mullin</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Beijing-based naval expert Li Jie said the PLA would learn from the experiences of its American counterpart in turning its LHD and LPD into mini-aircraft carrier strike groups, an effective cost-saving measure.</p><p>&#34;The US has studied how to operate their ARG in a more feasible and efficient way,&#34; Li said.</p><p>&#34;For China, the key mission of their Type 075 and Type 071 will be defending the country&#39;s territorial sovereignty in the East and South China seas, as well as overseas interests, meaning the ARG combination is a better option than aircraft carrier strike groups.&#34;</p><p>Macau-based military observer Antony Wong Tong said deploying both LHDs and LPDs indicated the US Navy&#39;s capacity for tactical manoeuvres and joint cooperation on the high seas.</p><p>&#34;The combination of LHD and LPD is an integrated expeditionary strike group, which is worth the PLA learning from if they are going to better deploy their Type 075 and Type 071 amphibious warships,&#34; Wong said.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5cc09f6fb14bf43f0879111a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"The Yimeng Shan, a Type 071 amphibious transport dock ship\" height=\"3235\" width=\"4841\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The Yimeng Shan, a Chinese navy Type 071 amphibious transport dock ship.\n<p class=\"copyright\">REUTERS/Jason Lee</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Beijing plans to own at least six aircraft carrier strike groups by 2035, but so far it just <a href=\"https://www.scmp.com/news/china/military/article/3128830/chinas-shandong-aircraft-carrier-ready-high-seas-test-insider\" data-v-2a60e86e=\"\">launched two</a>. The third is <a href=\"https://www.scmp.com/news/china/military/article/3093656/china-steps-shipbuilding-two-more-aircraft-carriers-under\" data-v-2a60e86e=\"\">expected to be completed</a> later this year.</p><p>China has launched three Type 075 LHDs, which were designed to each carry up to 30 attack helicopters and armoured vehicles, and eight smaller Type 071 LPDs with the displacement of 25,000 tonnes.</p><p>The Type 075 is the world&#39;s third largest amphibious assault vessel behind the USS Wasp and America classes. It is bigger than Japan&#39;s Izumo class and France&#39;s Mistral class.</p><p>However, Song said that in addition to the amphibious ships, the most powerful weapon of the Makin Island ARG were the F-35B squadrons and detachments of multi-role helicopters suited to different types of sea warfare missions.</p><p>&#34;The most challenging problem of the PLA is a lack of new-generation fixed-wing carrier-based aircraft like the F-35B Lightning II Joint Strike Fighter jets,&#34; Song said.</p><p>&#34;The F-35B helps the USS Marines grab air supremacy in both ARG operations, making its function like that of the mini-carrier strike groups … that means the US Navy owns nearly 20 carrier strike groups around the world.&#34;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5cc89d60e9f08a01e76ec8da?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Type 075 (rendering)\" height=\"1520\" width=\"2840\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A rendering of a Chinese Type 075 amphibious assault ship.\n<p class=\"copyright\">CCTV</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>To solve the current shortcomings, Song suggested the PLA install a catapult on the deck of the Type 075 LHD to upgrade the platform and allow it to operate the country&#39;s carrier-based J-15 fighter jet.</p><p>The US Navy was reported to have tested the idea of smaller carriers, which would reduce the range, speed and capacity of its US$13 billion nuclear-powered supercarriers known as CVNs, but cost half as much or even less, Forbes reported in December.</p><p>The ARG operation could be seen as testing a mini-carrier option, an exercise China could learn from, Song and Li said.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a to go public. </li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\"></a><strong><a target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Sign up here for our daily newsletter, 10 Things Before the Opening Bell.</a></strong></li>\n</ul><p>Shares of <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/coin-stock\">Coinbase</a> climbed as much as 13% on Wednesday in its hotly anticipated trading debut on the Nasdaq.</p><p>The direct listing had a $250-per-share reference price, and opened at $381 before hitting an intraday high of $429.54, which was 13% above its opening price.</p><p>The $381-per-share opening price put Coinbase&#39;s valuation at $99.5 billion, giving it a bigger market capitalization than such established US companies as General Motors, FedEx, and Gilead Sciences.</p><p>Coinbase is the first major cryptocurrency exchange to go public, and investors see its direct listing as a major milestone for bringing cryptocurrencies in the mainstream. <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/btc-usd?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Bitcoin</a> hovered near an all-time high above $63,000 when trading commenced, having hit a record of $64,869.77 earlier in the day.</p><p>&#34;We look at the Coinbase listing as an additional validation of the space, and a major PR opportunity for the entire industry to shine as the future of finance,&#34; said Alex Mashinsky, CEO and co-founder of Celsius, a cryptocurrency yield-earning platform.</p><p>He added: &#34;Coinbase has more users and more revenues than many of the largest Wall Street players and is more profitable than any major exchange, this validation puts most skeptics at a crossroads having to re-evaluate their denial and frustration with the disruption coming at them from all sides.&#34;</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/bitcoin-contango-offers-risk-free-high-return-trade-opportunity-futures-2021-4\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Bitcoin is a headache to store, and that&#39;s created an investment opportunity that could theoretically pay determined traders big risk-free returns by December</a></em></p><p>Coinbase&#39;s direct listing comes on the heels of its blowout first quarter earnings. The cryptocurrency exchange and brokerage <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/news/coinbase-q1-revenue-jump-bitcoin-crypto-market-too-volatile-forecast-2021-4-1030280362?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">revealed first quarter revenue grew 840% year-over-year to $1.8 billion,</a> compared to the $1.3 billion for all of 2020. </p><p>The results led <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/news/coinbase-price-target-raised-440-da-davidson-blockbuster-earnings-bitcoin-2021-4-1030282489\">DA Davidson analyst Gil Luria to up his price target for COIN to $440 from $195</a> .Though other analysts caution that Coinbase has hefty competition.</p><p><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/coinbase-direct-listing-valuation-billion-cryptocurrency-exchange-public-analysis-trainer-2021-3-1030169891\">David Trainer</a>, New Constructs CEO, said in a stock research note that Coinbase&#39;s $100 billion expected valuation implies that Coinbase will become the largest exchange in the world by revenue, which isn&#39;t guaranteed given the existence of competitors like Gemini, Kraken, and Binance.</p><p>In the earnings report, the company warned that its financial results have fluctuated drastically on swings in crypto trading volume-something investors should keep an eye on, Trainer said.</p><p>&#34;Trading volume, and therefore transaction revenue currently fluctuate, potentially materially, with Bitcoin price and crypto asset volatility. This revenue unpredictability, in turn, impacts our profitability on a quarter-to-quarter basis,&#34; Coinbase acknowledged in its prospectus.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article (Emily Graffeo)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/60763d7d74da0300181e1853?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn13@2020_3/2021/04/14/18-15-29-646_3d0a7c83466ce3b1.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn1@2020_2/2021/04/14/18-15-35-145_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=G_wx7lK5xJY:hsfuBZkJYfo:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn5@2020_5/2021/04/14/18-15-34-215_a57819f287d6577c.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=G_wx7lK5xJY:hsfuBZkJYfo:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn53@2020_3/2021/04/14/18-15-30-149_6d4c0485db090e39.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn29@2020_4/2021/04/14/18-15-29-996_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=G_wx7lK5xJY:hsfuBZkJYfo:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn13@2020_3/2021/04/14/18-15-34-226_767916c37cbfa84d.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/G_wx7lK5xJY":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn32@2020_3/2021/04/14/18-15-28-488_2de89acd0a35e033.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1618424108834},{"createdTime":"2021-04-15 02:15:08","updatedTime":"2021-04-15 02:15:08","title":"Ex-Navy SEAL and ultramarathoner David Goggins is the toughest man on the planet. His latest challenge: persuading the world to suffer on purpose.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/david-goggins-navy-seal-business-toughness-books-speaking-2021-4","description":"<p class=\"drop-cap\"></p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606c7ee42556c500189478cf?format=jpeg\" alt=\"david goggins turning joys of suffering into business model 2x1\" height=\"1250\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Brandon Rogers/US Navy; @davidgoggins/Twitter; Marianne Ayala/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p class=\"drop-cap\">Everywhere Devin Featherstone goes, David Goggins follows. It starts in the morning when Featherstone opens his eyes and catches Goggins&#39; thousand-yard stare from the book jacket of &#34;Can&#39;t Hurt Me,&#34; Goggins&#39; memoir, on his nightstand.</p><p>Throughout the day, Featherstone, 36, a firefighter and an avid runner in Calgary, Alberta, ingests YouTube videos and podcast clips of the former Navy SEAL and ultramarathoner, who reminds him to &#34;Stay hard!&#34; And as night falls, and Featherstone crawls back into bed beside his wife, there Goggins remains on the nightstand - inert, gazing blankly into the darkness.</p><p>Featherstone acknowledges the reality plainly: &#34;David Goggins is in my head daily.&#34;</p><p>The sway that Goggins, who is 46, has over his followers - his ability to occupy their thoughts and persuade them to push past their limits - is hard to overstate. Last month, he oversaw the Goggins Challenge, a two-day test of physical fitness that ran March 5-7. Across 90 countries, tens of thousands of weekend warriors ran four miles every four hours, for 48 hours straight. If you weren&#39;t a runner, you exercised. If you weren&#39;t a gym rat, you just got sweaty. It was free to enter, and if you wanted a T-shirt, you paid $35.</p><p>Devin Featherstone did it in full firefighter gear because why not.</p><p>While Goggins ended up donating more than $200,000 in profits from the T-shirt sales to charity, for individual people there is still no good reason to do challenges like these. But Goggins regularly inspires such action. Drawing on stories of his difficult past, mixed with expletive-ridden calls to reject creature comforts, he&#39;s found a way to become equal parts drill sergeant, life coach, and superhero for his community of nearly <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/davidgoggins/?hl=en\">4 million</a> highly engaged Instagram followers.</p><p>&#34;It&#39;s just really empowering,&#34; said Jenny Petersen, a 48-year-old nurse and runner from Lincoln, Nebraska, speaking of Goggins&#39; list of accomplishments. Petersen - a runner and triathlete - was among those who completed the Goggins Challenge. &#34;People are starting to embrace that it&#39;s OK if you suffer, and that you&#39;re tougher than you think.&#34;</p><p>After more than a year of both mental and physical anguish wrought by COVID-19, Goggins&#39; calls to embrace discomfort may seem ill-timed. But for the newly converted and die-hards alike, he&#39;s offering people more than motivation: an opportunity to reclaim control of their suffering, and practice it on their own terms.</p><p>Goggins&#39; fan base is growing fast, and there are promising signs his ability to monetize that interest - through a bestselling memoir, corporate speaking engagements, merchandise, and avenues yet-to-be explored - could carve out a lucrative &#34;business of toughness&#34; over the coming years.</p><p>&#34;I discovered a whole nother part of your fucking brain that a lot of people don&#39;t even know about,&#34; Goggins told Joe Rogan in a <a href=\"https://open.spotify.com/episode/70ssh8DCCOlwwOEAjLobW3?si=k0g4Ym4hTIulmEA2Tsl7mw\">2018 podcast episode</a>. &#34;It&#39;s my job now to take these weak people, in the category that I was in, and say, &#39;Uh-uh. Stop reading the bullshit. Stop listening to the bullshit.&#39; And if my story of success can impact somebody, it is my job, it is my duty, to share the story.&#34; (Goggins declined to be interviewed for this article.)</p><h2><strong>Achievements born from adversity</strong></h2><p class=\"drop-cap\">It was November 1, 2005, and a 6-foot-2, 245-pound linebacker of a Navy SEAL was on the starting line of a 24-hour footrace in Southern California. Goggins had signed up for the San Diego 1-Day, an event he entered as a qualifying race for a separate ultramarathon in which he hoped to raise money for charity.</p><p>He was no fleet-footed runner. In the lead-up to the race, Goggins&#39; cardiovascular training included just 20 minutes spent on the elliptical every Sunday. The task ahead of him: Complete 100 laps of the one-mile track before the 24 hours were up.</p><p>The race nearly broke Goggins, who describes the hellacious experience in his book and on podcasts as the most painful day of his life. He broke all the small bones in his feet. His kidneys shut down. By the time he got home, having run 101 miles in under 19 hours, he was smeared with blood, urine, and feces, and was unable to walk under his own weight. His wife at the time begged him to go to the hospital.</p><p>&#34;She kept talking, shouting, crying, trying to reach me through the haze,&#34; Goggins wrote in his 2018 memoir, &#34;Can&#39;t Hurt Me: Master Your Mind and Defy the Odds.&#34; &#34;And I heard most of what she said, but I knew if we went to the hospital they&#39;d give me pain killers and I didn&#39;t want to mask this pain. I&#39;d just accomplished the most amazing feat in my entire life.&#34;</p><bi-shortcode class=\"mceNonEditable\" data-type=\"image-spread\" data-image-count=\"3\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606cb09870954f0019195765?format=jpeg\" alt=\"brent gleeson &#38; david goggins\" height=\"825\" width=\"1099\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Navy SEAL training in 2001. Brent Gleeson, second from left. David Goggins, second from right.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Brent Gleeson</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure> <figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606cb11930004b0019b263e0?format=jpeg\" alt=\"david goggins\" height=\"828\" width=\"1105\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Goggins during Navy SEAL training.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Brent Gleeson</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure> <figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606cb12730004b0019b263e2?format=jpeg\" alt=\"David Goggins &#38; Brent Gleeson\" height=\"809\" width=\"1079\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Goggins and Gleeson at the SEAL training graduation in 2001.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Brent Gleeson</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></bi-shortcode><p>As Goggins described it, that race obliterated any sense of physical limits he&#39;d once had.</p><p>Two months after the San Diego 1-Day, he ran the Hurt 100, a 100-mile trail race with 24,500 feet of climbing through hills in Hawaii. In 2006, he completed seven more races of 30 miles or more. In 2007, he completed 14 more, including a third-place finish at the Badwater 135, a race longer than five normal marathons that cuts through the sneaker-melting heat of Death Valley. He&#39;s completed two dozen more ultras in the 14 years since.</p><p>Goggins has also competed in the Ironman World Championship, finishing the 140.6-mile triathlon in 11 hours and 24 minutes. And in 2013, he broke the Guinness World Record for most pullups completed in 24 hours with 4,030. He broke the record with seven hours to spare.</p><p>For people such as Petersen and Featherstone, Goggins&#39; core appeal is his mental toughness, which Goggins said he channels into <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/p/B0jC_nzns2X/\">&#34;going the distance,&#34;</a> not winning the race. He speaks often of the &#34;40% rule,&#34; which says that when people typically give up, they&#39;re really only 40% depleted.</p><p>&#34;The reason it&#39;s so powerful,&#34; Goggins wrote in &#34;Can&#39;t Hurt Me,&#34; &#34;is that if you follow it, you will unlock your mind to new levels of performance and excellence in sports and in life, and your rewards will run far deeper than mere material success.&#34;</p><p>The San Diego 1-Day marked Goggins&#39; first step on the road to becoming an endurance athlete, but overcoming adversity stretches back to his childhood. Growing up Black in the small, predominantly white town of Brazil, Indiana, he faced virulent racism and struggled with a learning disability, speech impediment, and low self-esteem.</p><p>&#34;I damn sure wasn&#39;t going to get into college based on academics,&#34; Goggins wrote in &#34;Can&#39;t Hurt Me.&#34; &#34;All I knew was that I had to get the fuck out of Brazil, Indiana.&#34; He saw the military as his best chance and took the requisite entrance exam three times. On his third try, he met the minimum standard for the Air Force.</p><p>To date, Goggins is the only person to complete training as a Navy SEAL, Army Ranger, and Air Force Tactical Air Controller. And &#34;when that glory faded,&#34; about 20 years ago, Goggins set his sights on ultramarathon running, said Brent Gleeson, a former Navy SEAL who graduated from SEAL training with Goggins in 2001.</p><p>&#34;He&#39;s always striving, as he would say, to recertify himself as a savage,&#34; said Gleeson, who is now an entrepreneur and the author of several books, including &#34;Embrace the Suck: The Navy SEAL Way to an Extraordinary Life.&#34; &#34;It&#39;s that continual journey, and I think that inadvertently started to spark something in other people.&#34;</p><p>Even in middle age, Goggins seems to have no plans of slowing down. In October, at 45 years old, he ran 238 miles in 62 hours, 21 minutes, and 29 seconds as part of the Moab 240 in Utah. It was good enough for a second-place finish.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606cb1f570954f0019195778?format=jpeg\" alt=\"David Goggins by Brandon Rogers:US Navy\" height=\"1391\" width=\"1855\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Goggins ran the Badwater 135 in 2007, in a string of 14 ultramarathon races that year.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Brandon Rogers/US Navy</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h2><strong>Not just transformation - multiplication</strong></h2><p>But now the 46-year-old veteran is increasingly turning his attention toward brand-building. In 2016, Goggins, along with his team, founded Goggins LLC as a way to start investing in himself, as he told Rogan on his first of two podcast appearances.</p><p>&#34;I try to be as real as I can,&#34; Goggins said, &#34;because we&#39;re all fucking suffering in this world. We&#39;re all hurting. And I try to take away all titles you wanna give me to let you know that I did not come from that shit. That&#39;s why I have to be so authentic and so real about my own insecurities and my own faults, and being a fucked-up person.&#34;</p><p>Influencers strive to be as authentic as possible; it can <a href=\"https://blog.hootsuite.com/authentic-social-media/\">make or break</a> a nascent brand. Fortunately for Goggins, who may never even use the word &#34;influencer,&#34; staying true to himself and his story has been the greatest source of his success - and sometimes his stress.</p><p>&#34;My biggest fear in life is, people can read right through a motherfucker that&#39;s not real,&#34; he told Rogan. &#34;I do it all the time. A lot of people have these great quotes, and they mass-produce. I can&#39;t mass-produce something, man.&#34;</p><p>Instead, he&#39;s started giving talks. He&#39;s spoken at companies such as Cisco and Microsoft and at pro sports teams such as the Seattle Seahawks and the New York Giants. (Because of COVID-19, he has not given a talk since March 2020, a spokesperson confirmed.) Clips from these talks carry titles such as &#34;Stop Talking Yourself Out of Being Great&#34; and &#34;Get Comfortable With Being Uncomfortable.&#34;</p><p>There is ample room for Goggins to grow in these spaces: Together, the <a href=\"https://blog.marketresearch.com/the-10-billion-self-improvement-market-adjusts-to-new-generation\">self-improvement</a> and <a href=\"https://blog.marketresearch.com/u.s.-motivational-speaking-market-worth-1.9-billion\">motivational-speaking</a> markets are worth about $15 billion. And they are expected to grow between 4% and 6% over the next few years, according to research from Marketdata Enterprises.</p><p>In 2018, he and his co-author, Adam Skolnick, self-published his memoir, &#34;Can&#39;t Hurt Me.&#34; He said in a <a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/NickJamesExpertEmpires/videos/845740925804974/\">2019 Facebook Live event</a> that, despite being offered an advance of $300,000, he turned it down &#34;at the last minute&#34; and decided instead to invest $800,000 of his own money in self-publishing. (Goggins&#39; press representative did not respond to Insider&#39;s request to confirm these figures.)</p><p>&#34;It was the best decision, business-wise, I ever made in my entire life,&#34; Goggins said in the event, &#34;because I had the mental toughness and also the ability to know what was right for me and my brand.&#34;</p><p>The book ended up selling 900,000 copies across print and digital within the first four months, Deadline&#39;s Patrick Hipes <a href=\"https://deadline.com/2019/04/david-goggins-cant-hurt-me-hollywood-agency-wme-1202604800/\">reported</a>. It stayed on The New York Times&#39; bestseller list for 14 weeks and has sold more than 3 million copies to date. According to Bookscan data, roughly 300,000 of those copies are from the two bound editions.</p><p>&#34;That&#39;s spectacular for any book,&#34; said Giles Anderson, the owner and founder of Anderson Literary Agency.</p><p>Still, even as a businessman, Goggins is adamant that money isn&#39;t what gets him up in the morning. &#34;I&#39;m not driven by the business,&#34; he told Rogan. &#34;I&#39;m a minimalist motherfucker. Gimme a backpack, a fucking ground to sleep on, a pullup bar, some fucking running shoes, and a Subway sandwich, and I&#39;m fucking straight.&#34;</p><p>To be sure, Goggins isn&#39;t the only tough-as-nails influencer. Plenty have come before him, Tony Robbins perhaps looming the largest, literally, over the past two decades. Nor is Goggins the only veteran turned life coach to break onto the scene in recent years.</p><p>Jocko Willink is a retired naval officer, a podcaster, and the author of several books, including &#34;Extreme Ownership: How Navy SEALs Lead and Win.&#34; Willink is well known on Instagram, where he has nearly 2 million followers, for posting gritty, black-and-white close-ups of his digital watch displaying ungodly wake-up times. A recent photo <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/p/CNFOaKlDQ8u/\">showed the time</a> as 4:25:41. The caption: &#34;WARPATH.&#34;</p><p>Many of Goggins&#39; followers also find strength in Jocko, as he&#39;s better known. But where Jocko has posted more than 4,700 times, Goggins has just 335 posts to his name, and each one is a viral sensation in its own right. His videos regularly pull in more than a million views.</p><p>To retired SEAL Gleeson, who previously founded and ran a digital-media agency for 11 years, the growth and engagement Goggins has achieved are nothing short of anomalous. &#34;I&#39;ve never seen an explosion of rapid growth from a social-media-brand standpoint,&#34; Gleeson said. &#34;Never seen it before.&#34;</p><bi-shortcode class=\"mceNonEditable\" data-type=\"image-spread\" data-image-count=\"2\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606cb53e70954f00191957aa?format=jpeg\" alt=\"david goggins moab 240\" height=\"1160\" width=\"890\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Goggins ran the Moab 240 in October, finishing second.\n<p class=\"copyright\">David Goggins/Instagram</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure> <figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606cb56070954f00191957ac?format=jpeg\" alt=\"david goggins moab 240\" height=\"1120\" width=\"908\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Goggins&#39; finishing time at the Moab 240 was 62 hours, 21 minutes.\n<p class=\"copyright\">David Goggins/Instagram</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></bi-shortcode><h2><strong>Goggins isn&#39;t for everyone … yet</strong></h2><p>Part of Goggins&#39; appeal has been the mythic quality that&#39;s followed him ever since stories began to surface on YouTube about six years ago. In 2015, the entrepreneur Jesse Itzler published &#34;Living With a SEAL: 31 Days Training With the Toughest Man on the Planet.&#34; Itzler never used the SEAL&#39;s name in the book, but word soon got out that the &#34;toughest man&#34; was in fact David Goggins. More videos emerged; rumors swirled. <em>Have you heard of David Goggins?</em> The man himself began appearing on podcasts, news shows, and social media.</p><p>All that organic growth has created a reputation that some find intriguing. For instance, a month after the official Goggins Challenge weekend in March, <a href=\"https://www.runnersworld.com/runners-stories/a36048798/zac-clark-david-goggins-48-hour-challenge/\">a handful of New York City-based runners</a> embarked on the challenge to raise money for charity the weekend of April 9. For others, who may be landing on Goggins&#39; Instagram page for the first time, the catalog of running videos, in which our hero yells at the camera for a minute straight, may seem intimidating. But for every Goggins nonbeliever, there is often a friend close by who&#39;s ready to dispel the myths and spread the gospel.</p><p>Joelle Tomlinson, a morning-news host in Calgary, and a friend of Featherstone, regularly runs ultramarathons. When she came across Goggins, in 2020, by way of a running partner, she first thought, &#34;Wow, this guy is absolutely wild&#34; - in a good way, she said. &#34;I&#39;ve never heard of anyone like this. I think he has completely made this recreational suffering more achievable.&#34; She said she was eager to pick up a copy of his book.</p><p>But then there are people such as Jacy Cunningham, a 32-year-old professional trainer in Maryland, who admire Goggins for his intensity but find less value in glorifying it as a way of life. &#34;Our society promotes pure extreme,&#34; said Cunningham, who runs his own business on a holistic form of fitness called the Jacy Method. &#34;We&#39;re fanatic about crazy shit. We&#39;re big on pushing ourselves to crazy limits.&#34;</p><p>Devin Featherstone said an increasingly comfortable world is to blame. &#34;People are driving more toward that in-your-face attitude of how Goggins tells you straight up: If you&#39;re lazy, you&#39;re lazy. You&#39;re not candy-coating it, and I think more and more people need that.&#34;</p><p>Still, even a superfan such as Featherstone said he&#39;s motivated most by his family and his values, and that he taps the fearless warrior in his head only when times get tough. As a dad to a 5-year-old son, he knows the misery of a 4 a.m. wake-up. But after studying &#34;Can&#39;t Hurt Me&#34; and listening to clip after clip, Featherstone said cleaning a mess or settling a dispute doesn&#39;t seem so bad.</p><p>&#34;There are things that I would bitch and complain about that were really small,&#34; he said. Now, not so much, and people have even asked where his inner peace comes from. &#34;I&#39;m, like, &#39;Honestly? I read David Goggins&#39; book.&#39;&#34;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a @2020_1/2021/04/14/18-15-29-990_461ab5c1aca276df.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/_kCDsWl6Vns":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn22@2020_6/2021/04/14/18-15-30-065_c068ce7adca19d9d.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1618424108869},{"createdTime":"2021-04-15 02:15:08","updatedTime":"2021-04-15 02:15:08","title":"How Honolulu, Hawaii is working toward sustainability and supporting its residents in the process","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/honolulu-hawaii-sustainability-climate-change-renewable-energy-2021-4","description":"<div class=\"content-header\"><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/advancing-cities\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/603e678a13b221001876b17b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Advancing cities banner v3\" height=\"314\" width=\"2501\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></a></p></div><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/607064dbf068cf0018022bd5?format=jpeg\" alt=\"005.JPG\" height=\"2014\" width=\"2680\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Solar panels on top of homes in a Honolulu neighborhood.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Resilience Office</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Honolulu has been focused on sustainability and climate change since receiving a grant in 2016.</li>\n<li>Its resilience plan has promoted access to renewable energy and expanded clean transportation.</li>\n<li>Other initiatives include reducing energy bills and addressing hunger by supporting local farmers. </li>\n<li id=\"recirc\">This article is part of a series focused on American cities building a better tomorrow called &#34;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/advancing-cities\">Advancing Cities</a>.&#34;</li>\n</ul><p>In his <a href=\"https://www.hawaiinewsnow.com/2021/03/14/heres-how-watch-mayor-blangiardis-first-state-city-address/\">first state-of-the-city speech</a> in mid-March, Rick Blangiardi, mayor of Honolulu, Hawaii, emphasized the city&#39;s commitment to &#34;climate resilience.&#34; </p><p>&#34;From sea level rise, rain bombs, and increasing temperatures, we&#39;re taking steps toward a climate-ready Oahu,&#34; said the mayor, who was sworn in at the start of 2021. The island of Oahu is home to the city and county of Honolulu. </p><p>&#34;We&#39;re shifting from talking about policy to doing something about it,&#34; Blangiardi added. </p><p>Sustainability and climate change are issues that Honolulu&#39;s leaders have been working to address for years. In 2016, the city was awarded a <a href=\"https://www.rockefellerfoundation.org/news/100-resilient-cities-rockefeller-foundation-announce-37-new-member-cities-reaching-100-city-milestone-global-network/\">100 Resilient Cities Initiative Grant</a> from the Rockefeller Foundation to help fund the hiring of a chief resilience officer to work with the city on crafting climate change and resilience plans. </p><p>Since then, Honolulu has debuted a Resilience Strategy and a Climate Action Plan, which have helped inspire citywide legislation to reduce the energy burden on residents, promote access to renewable energy, expand clean transportation, and support locally grown food producers. </p><p>Here&#39;s a look at some of Honolulu&#39;s sustainability initiatives.</p>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\tCodifying the Resilience Office's responsibilities will help Honolulu meet its sustainability goals\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/607059be30004b0019b26d7e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Oʻahu Resilience Strategy Steering Committee members meeting during development phase of the strategy, which includes Honolulu Mayor Rick Blangiardi.\" height=\"1152\" width=\"1536\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Oahu Resilience Strategy Steering Committee members meeting during the development phase of the strategy, which includes Honolulu Mayor Rick Blangiardi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Resilience Office</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The <a href=\"https://resilientoahu.org/\">Office of Climate Change, Sustainability and Resiliency</a> was created by a city charter amendment that was approved by the public in 2016. A <a href=\"https://resilientoahu.org/bills\">new bill signed</a> into law in December 2020 \"codifies the duties, responsibilities, and reporting requirements\" of the office to ensure Honolulu meets its climate change and sustainability goals.&#160;</p><p>Bill 65 establishes an <a href=\"https://www.nrdc.org/experts/elizabeth-stampe/honolulu-climate-laws-will-reduce-driving-and-save-energy\">energy benchmarking system</a>, requiring Honolulu to create and report energy and water use benchmarks for city-owned buildings. The rule is estimated to save the city $7 million over the next decade. The bill also specifies that the city will transition to 100% renewable energy and become carbon neutral by 2045.&#160;&#160;</p><p>It also addresses many other climate change and sustainability measures, including a One Water policy, examining efficiencies across the city's water system.&#160;</p>\n\tThe Resilience Strategy addresses affordability and climate change\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60705a2730004b0019b26d83?format=jpeg\" alt=\"002.JPG\" height=\"1134\" width=\"1511\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The Resilience Office engaging community members on their perspectives of &#34;Resilience.&#34;\n<p class=\"copyright\">Resilience Office</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>One of the central initiatives of the Resilience Office is the <a href=\"https://online.flowpaper.com/74d206f1/OlaResilienceStrategy/#page=1\">Oahu Resilience Strategy</a>, which aims to address \"long-term affordability and the impacts of a climate crisis that is already driving islanders from their homes,\" according to the office's website.&#160;</p><p>Planning began in 2017 when the office met with Oahu's 33 neighborhood boards to survey residents about what concerned them most about climate change and how they thought it could be addressed, Matthew Gonser, chief resilience officer and executive director of Honolulu's Office of Climate Change, Sustainability and Resiliency, told Insider.&#160;</p><p>Hundreds of ideas were gathered from the community. Those concepts were narrowed down into 44 actions, comprising the Resilience Strategy. The strategy focuses on four broad subjects: long-term affordability, natural disaster preparedness and response, climate change, and local community leadership.&#160;</p><p>By the end of 2020, significant progress had been made on about half of the 44 resilience actions, Gonser said.</p>\n\tThe Climate Action Plan outlines what's needed to address climate change long term\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60705a9a30004b0019b26d89?format=jpeg\" alt=\"008\" height=\"3996\" width=\"5328\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The City and County of Honolulu Climate Action Plan open house community engagement session with Hawaii Pacific University and the Chamber of Commerce Hawaii.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Resilience Office</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Honolulu's Resilience Office released the city's <a href=\"https://resilientoahu.org/climate-action-plan\">Climate Action Plan</a> in December 2020.</p><p>The plan was developed based on scientific evidence and community input to fight climate change and reduce fossil fuel emissions on Oahu. It spells out the needed programs, policies, and actions for the city to become carbon neutral by 2045 &#8212; and includes nine strategies to focus on over the next five years, including increasing renewable energy and energy efficiency.&#160;</p><p>To develop the Climate Action Plan, community meetings with Honolulu City Council members, Hawaii Pacific University, the University of Hawaii at Mānoa, and the Chamber of Commerce of Hawaii were held, and working groups with stakeholders were set up, Gonser said.&#160;</p><p>During the first few months of 2021, the public had the chance to share their opinions and concerns about the plan before it goes to the city council. Gonser said the Climate Action Plan will likely be adopted this year.&#160;</p>\n\tHonolulu updated parking ordinances to promote walkability and the use of clean energy transportation\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60705b324d3e410018b70357?format=jpeg\" alt=\"006\" height=\"2660\" width=\"3547\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Jeff Mikulina, executive director of Blue Planet, speaking at the signing of Ordinance 20-41, related to off-street parking and loading.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Resilience Office</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>At the end of 2020, former mayor Kirk Caldwell signed Bill 2 to <a href=\"https://static1.squarespace.com/static/5e3885654a153a6ef84e6c9c/t/604fa68223340550a755dbff/1615832709176/Parking+and+Loading+Ord+20-41.pdf\">update Honolulu's mandatory parking requirements</a> for new developments. It gives developers more flexibility in how much parking to build and allows opportunities for the land to be used for other purposes, such as affordable housing.&#160;</p><p>\"It's making sure that our rules and regulations don't force overbuilding of parking, empowering more choice and leaving it to developers to determine what's needed,\" Gonser said.&#160;</p><p>The bill supports walkable neighborhoods and cleaner transportation options, such as biking and public transportation, which Honolulu plans to transition to clean fuel.&#160;</p><p>It could also make housing more affordable since constructing and maintaining parking is sometimes a hidden cost for renters, according to an <a href=\"https://ulupono.com/news-listing/report-reveals-the-hidden-costs-of-parking-in-hawaii/\">analysis by the Ulupono Initiative</a>, a Honolulu-based organization that provides grants, investments, and advocacy to support renewable energy, locally produced food, and other sustainability-minded projects.</p><p>For urban Honolulu renters, up to 37% of their rent may go toward parking, which, for decades, has often been built based on city regulation rather than actual need.&#160;&#160;&#160;</p><p>\"The bill makes progress in the right direction, better aligning with city climate and community goals, while allowing parking to remain accessible for those who genuinely need it and not requiring it of those who don't,\" Kathleen Rooney, Ulupono Initiative's director of transportation policy and programs, said <a href=\"https://ulupono.com/news-listing/bill-2-puts-honolulu-on-the-road-to-rightsizing-parking/\">when the bill was signed</a>.&#160;</p>\n\tMaking solar power more accessible eases Honolulu's energy burden\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60705baf4d3e410018b7035b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Solar array installation on top of the Board of Water Supply, City and County of Honolulu\" height=\"981\" width=\"1310\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Solar array installation on top of the Board of Water Supply.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Resilience Office</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Hawaii has one of the highest average electricity retail prices in the country, according to the <a href=\"https://www.eia.gov/state/?sid=HI#tabs-5\">US Energy Information Administration</a>, and the state relies on petroleum for most of its electricity generation.&#160;</p><p>Reducing the energy burden is a key focus area of Honolulu's Resilience Office. In December, the <a href=\"https://www.staradvertiser.com/2020/12/24/breaking-news/caldwell-signs-three-bills-addressing-parking-solar-permitting-and-climate-change/\">city enacted Bill 58</a> to streamline the permitting process for residential clean energy products, such as solar power, energy storage, and electric vehicle chargers. The goal is to cut down on the costs and time it takes to install solar systems.&#160;</p><p>Creating more equitable access to renewable energy is an important component in making Honolulu an affordable place to live, Gonser said.&#160;</p><p>\"We have one of the highest energy burdens in the nation,\" he said. \"It's updating our energy code and making sure that all new things that are being built are ensuring long-term affordability for residents and that they can benefit from progressive infrastructure so that we can reduce the energy burden over time.\"</p>\n\tNew performance-based regulations could lower energy bills for residents\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60705c474d3e410018b70362?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Infographic HPUC Timeline with PBR\" height=\"3300\" width=\"5100\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A timeline of the Hawaiian Public Utilities Commission.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Ulupono Initiative</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>As another initiative aimed at reducing energy bills, Hawaii's Public Utilities Commission <a href=\"https://puc.hawaii.gov/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/PBR-Phase-2-DO.Page-Press-Release.Final_.12-22-2020.pdf\">approved a new Performance-Based Regulation Framework</a> in late 2020. The framework would transform utility company Hawaiian Electric by making its operations more efficient, lowering electricity rates, improving services, and meeting the state's clean energy goals.&#160;</p><p>\"That's really groundbreaking,\" Amy Hennessy, senior vice president of communications and external affairs at Ulupono Initiative, which <a href=\"https://ulupono.com/news-listing/white-paper-performance-based-regulation/\">provided research</a> and other information to guide the framework's adoption, told Insider. \"The impacts toward changing the incentives for our utility to transform into a renewable energy future are significant.\"&#160;</p><p>The new structure provides <a href=\"https://www.staradvertiser.com/2020/12/28/hawaii-news/hawaiian-electric-bills-to-drop-under-new-puc-rules/?HSA=a11bdd3aa7748a6352ba20b771c9a0cc17f0017c\">financial incentives</a> for the electric company to meet certain goals, like creating savings for lower-income customers and reducing greenhouse gases. It also separates the utility's profits from capital investments, creating a cost-of-service approach.&#160;</p>\n\tMatching grant provides $1 million to fight hunger and support local food producers\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60705cf430004b0019b26d94?format=jpeg\" alt=\"DSC_8846\" height=\"4010\" width=\"5347\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The Hawaii Farm Bureau.\n<p class=\"copyright\">The Hawaii Farm Bureau</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p><a href=\"https://www.kitv.com/story/43562413/many-hawaii-families-face-food-insecurity-during-the-pandemic\">Hunger</a> has been an ongoing problem for many communities, but the pandemic worsened the situation, as unemployment increased and many families have faced new financial struggles.&#160;</p><p>To address hunger in Hawaii, Gov. David Ige announced in October 2020 that the state would provide a <a href=\"https://governor.hawaii.gov/newsroom/latest-news/office-of-the-governor-news-release-government-private-sector-partnership-double-food-bucks-to-help-hawaii-families-and-local-agriculture/\">$500,000 matching donation</a> to the <a href=\"https://dabux.org/\">DA BUX Double Up Food Bucks program</a>, which doubles the amount of the Supplemental Nutrition Assistance Program (SNAP) benefits, formerly known as food stamps, that are spent on locally grown food.&#160;</p><p>Several private-sector organizations raised $500,000 for the program, including the <a href=\"https://stupski.org/\">Stupski Foundation</a> and Ulupono Initiative, which each provided $200,000. The state match offers $1 million total for the program.&#160;</p><p>Addressing hunger and providing incentives to encourage residents to buy more locally grown and produced food are part of Honolulu's Resilience Strategy. The DA BUX Double Up Food Bucks program also aims to strengthen the local economy because it keeps residents' food budgets on the island.</p><p>\"A million dollars going out into communities for not just those who need access to food, but also our local farmers who needed a market &#8212; it's actually putting dollars in their pockets while they're growing to help provide healthy options for the community,\" Hennessy said. \"So it's really a triple win.\"</p>\n</div><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a soothing different types of pain and can provide relief within minutes. Some uses for heating pads include relieving aches from sports injuries, gym workouts, mild arthritis, menstrual cramps, and general tightness from sitting in front of a desk for prolonged periods. </p><p>A common concern is that you&#39;ll fall asleep with the heating pad on, increasing your risk of burns or skin irritation. To combat this, most heating pads automatically shut off, though you can sometimes override this feature. In addition, many have a variety of temperature settings to choose from. </p><p>If you&#39;re concerned about pain relief, you&#39;ll want to look at heating pads that provide moist and dry heat therapy. According to a 2015 BioMed Central <a href=\"https://trialsjournal.biomedcentral.com/articles/10.1186/s13063-015-0800-4\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">study</a>, heat therapy helps with blood flow and metabolism, helps to decrease muscle tension, and helps to improve range of motion. </p><p>Some heating pads qualify as eligible flex spending account (FSA) expenses, so if you have funds to use up, a heating pad is an option to consider.</p><h2>Here are the best heating pads of 2021</h2><ul class=\"summary-list\"><li><strong>Best heating pad overall: <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B01KVYJJA6/ref=as_li_tl?ie=UTF8&tag=biip_041421_best-heating-pad-20&camp=1789&creative=9325&linkCode=as2&creativeASIN=B01KVYJJA6&linkId=1c1cbab34ed278015aeb9525e28a42404ed278015aeb9525e28a4240\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow sponsored\">Sunbeam XpressHeat Heating Pad</a></strong></li><li><strong>Best budget heating pad: <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.target.com%2Fp%2Fking-heating-pad-up-38-up-8482%2F-%2FA-81063090\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow sponsored\">Up &#38; src=\"https://i.insider.com/6076f0e574da0300181e1923?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Coinbase Founder and CEO Brian Armstrong\" height=\"1602\" width=\"3205\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Coinbase Founder and CEO Brian Armstrong\n<p class=\"copyright\">Steven Ferdman/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><br>\n<ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Companies with bitcoin exposure jumped on Wednesday ahead of the direct listing of Coinbase.</li>\n<li>The rise is in lockstep with the broader rally in cryptocurrencies.  </li>\n<li>&#34;The Coinbase IPO is being met with excitement that global crypto market cap will grow by at least 50% later this year,&#34; an analyst said.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://newsletter.businessinsider.com/join/4np/10-things-opening-bell\">Sign up here for our daily newsletter, 10 Things Before the Opening Bell</a></li>\n</ul><p>Companies with bitcoin exposure jumped on Wednesday in lockstep with the broader cryptocurrency rally ahead of the highly anticipated direct listing of Coinbase. </p><p>&#34;The Coinbase IPO is being met with excitement that global crypto market cap will grow by at least 50% later this year,&#34; Edward Moya, senior analyst at OANDA, told Insider. &#34;Each legitimate investment vehicle for cryptocurrencies is solidifying the belief that this bubble won&#39;t come crashing down to zero.&#34; </p><p>&#34;All four of these have a direct benefit from bitcoin being up,&#34; John Wu, president of Ava Labs, the company beside altcoin Avalanche, told Insider. &#34;Others like PayPal who help facilitate the trading of crypto are up because of sentiment but they don&#39;t actually own bitcoin.&#34;</p><p>Wu said the stocks are now trading lower since investors are &#34;buying the hype, selling the fact&#34;. He added that investors may now be allocating ay from these names to the cryptocurrencies themselves.</p><p>Coinbase CEO Brian Armstrong on Wednesday <a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/video/2021/04/14/coinbase-ceo-brian-amrstrong-company-valuation-bitcoin.html\">during his interview with CNBC</a> made the case as to why the public should invest in his firm rather than straight to the cryptocurrencies.</p><p>&#34;We are kind of what you might call an index bet or a levered bet on the crypto space more broadly,&#34; he said.</p><p>Tesla on February 8 disclosed its <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/news/tesla-buys-bitcoin-elon-musk-stock-accept-form-of-payment-2021-2-1030055107?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest&_ga=2.243402565.1525180420.1618406257-1338790433.161798633117986331\">$1.5 billion bitcoin investment</a>, according to a <a href=\"https://ir.tesla.com/_flysystem/s3/sec/000156459021004599/tsla-10k_20201231-gen.pdf\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">regulatory filing.</a> Elon Musk&#39;s company followed up with an announcement the next month that <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-tweets-you-can-buy-a-tesla-with-bitcoin-2021-3\">people can now buy a Tesla car with bitcoin</a>. </p><p>MicroStrategy, meanwhile, holds the record as the <a href=\"https://finance.yahoo.com/news/microstrategy-becomes-first-listed-company-113746283.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">first publicly listed company</a> to buy bitcoin as part of its capital allocation strategy in August 2020. It&#39;s since bought billions worth of the coin on multiple occasions and currently holds $5.4 billion, according to a <a href=\"https://www.sec.gov/ix?doc=/Archives/edgar/data/0001050446/000119312521105625/d113059d8k.htm\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">regulatory filing</a>. In April, Michael Saylor&#39;s firm announced that it is <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/news/microstrategy-mstr-pay-board-directors-entirely-bitcoin-btc-michael-saylor-2021-4-1030294660?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">paying non-employee board members</a> entirely in <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/btc-usd?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestedium=ingest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">bitcoin</a> instead of cash.</p><p>As for Square, its founder and CEO Jack Dorsey has long been one of the staunchest advocates of bitcoin. In <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/news/tesla-buys-bitcoin-elon-musk-stock-accept-form-of-payment-2021-2-1030055107?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest&_ga=2.243402565.1525180420.1618406257-1338790433.161798633117986331\">October 2020</a>, Square<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/bitcoin-price-square-buys-million-ubiquitious-potential-currency-digital-tech-2020-10?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestm=ingest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> announced</a> it had purchased 4,709 <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/btc-usd?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">bitcoins</a> for an aggregate price of $50 million. The San Francisco-based company paid an average price of $10,617 for each bitcoin.</p><p>The Coinbase direct listing on the Nasdaq prompted a broader cryptocurrency rally.</p><p><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/btc-usd?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingesttm_medium=ingest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"de63ece5dea514357e9bbcec1c3bdf50\">Bitcoin</a> broke its record for the third straight day, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/news/bitcoin-price-record-high-coinbase-direct-listing-btc-crypto-2021-4-1030302632\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">soaring to an all-time high above $65,000</a> Wednesday. <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/eth-usd?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingesttm_medium=ingest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Ether</a> <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/news/ether-price-all-time-high-coinbase-listing-berlin-hard-fork-2021-4-1030300075?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestm=ingest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">spiked as much as 8% to a new record high</a>, hitting a $250 billion market capitalization for the first time on Tuesday. <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/doge-usd?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestedium=ingest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Dogecoin</a> hit new records as well, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/news/dogecoin-price-today-record-high-market-capitalization-doge-meme-cryptocurrency-2021-4-1030300256?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestm=ingest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">jumping 34%</a> to a valuation of $11 billion.</p><p>&#34;Bitcoin and the other top altcoins are making fresh record highs as large parts of Wall Street are finally drinking the Kool-Aid,&#34; Moya said. </p><p>The Coinbase direct listing is viewed by many cryptocurrency advocates as a milestone for the digital ecosystem as it looks to continue to make headway into mainstream financial markets.</p><p>&#34;Coinbase is the first crypto company to make mainstream waves and is already valued higher than historic financial institutions like JP Morgan. This, coinciding with crypto&#39;s market cap surpassing 2 trillion, provides the space with much-needed stability that will reassure retail investors,&#34; Ganesh Swami, co-founder and CEO of Covalent, a provider of blockchain data, told Insider.</p><p>The stocks were all up during premarket trading but had pared some gains late Wednesday morning. Here&#39;s where the stocks traded as of 10:51 a.m. ET:</p><ul><li>Tesla down 0.37 to $759.00</li><li>MicroStrategy up 5.52% to $801.72</li><li>Square up $2.47% to $266.52</li><li>Galaxy Digital $45,000","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/2022-audi-q4-e-tron-ev-crossover-price-specs-features-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6077296274da0300181e1ab1?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Audi Q4 E-Tron.\" height=\"1874\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Audi Q4 E-Tron.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Audi</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Audi unveiled two new electric crossovers on Wednesday: the 2022 Q4 E-Tron and Q4 E-Tron Sportback. </li>\n<li>The base model will cost under $45,000 and have a range of around 250 miles, Audi said. </li>\n<li>The twin EVs will hit US dealerships toward the end of 2021. </li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Audi on Wednesday <a href=\"https://www.audi-mediacenter.com/en/electric-suvs-in-the-premium-compact-segment-the-audi-q4-e-tron-and-the-q4-sportback-e-tron-13887\">unveiled</a> a pair of new electric crossovers: the 2022 Q4 E-Tron and Q4 E-Tron Sportback. Their addition to Audi&#39;s lineup slashes the entry price for an Audi electric vehicle by more than $20,000.</p><p>The two EVs will hit US dealer lots toward the end of 2021 with a starting MSRP of less than $45,000, Audi says. And that&#39;s before the federal tax incentive that could effectively knock the price down another $7,500. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6077296242061500181757b4?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Audi Q4 E-Tron Sportback.\" height=\"1407\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Audi Q4 E-Tron Sportback.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Audi</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The two models are essentially twins, with the Sportback version aimed at customers interested in sacrificing a bit of trunk space for a roof that slants down in the back. Audi says they&#39;re roughly the same size as its gas-powered Q5 SUV.</p><p>They&#39;re Audi&#39;s fourth and fifth battery-powered vehicles for the US market, after the larger E-Tron and E-Tron Sportback crossovers and the E-Tron GT sport sedan. A 2021 E-Tron will run you at least $66,000. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6077296274da0300181e1ab0?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Audi Q4 E-Tron Sportback.\" height=\"1407\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Audi Q4 E-Tron Sportback.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Audi</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The entry-level, single-motor Q4 40 E-Tron will be able to travel around 250 miles on a charge, according to Audi&#39;s estimates. That range puts it in the same wheelhouse as many other EVs on the market, but behind Tesla, whose &#34;Long Range&#34; Model Y crossover has an EPA-estimated range of 326 miles. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6077296274da0300181e1ab2?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Audi Q4 E-Tron.\" height=\"1666\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Audi Q4 E-Tron.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Audi</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>There will also be a Q4 50 E-Tron and a Q4 50 E-Tron Sportback, which come equipped with an extra motor powering the front wheels. Those models will put out 295 horsepower, compared to the base version&#39;s roughly 200. </p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/elon-musk-wants-tesla-big-in-texas-terrible-idea-2021-4\">Elon Musk wants Tesla to be big in Texas. That might just be a terrible idea.</a></em></p><p>Audi didn&#39;t release range figures for the dual-motor Q4 models but said they will be nearly as efficient as the single-motor version thanks to a system that switches on all-wheel drive only when the extra power or traction is needed. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6077296074da0300181e1aaf?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Audi Q4 E-Tron.\" height=\"1874\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Audi Q4 E-Tron.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Audi</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Inside, buyers get a 10.1-inch touchscreen display and a 10.25-inch digital instrument cluster as standard, and those desiring more screen can opt for a larger 11.6-inch display.</p><p>Audi is also offering an augmented-reality display that shows some driver-assist and navigation information as if it&#39;s floating in front of the windshield. A Sonos sound system is available too. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6077296242061500181757b6?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Audi Q4 E-Tron.\" height=\"1666\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Audi Q4 E-Tron.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Audi</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The duo of lower-cost EVs is all part of Audi&#39;s plan to have 30% of its global lineup be electrified (that is, fully electric or hybrid) by 2025. Audi says it plans to have more fully electric models on the US market than any other luxury brand by the end of 2021 - and it&#39;s making good headway toward that goal. BMW currently only sells the i3 hatchback, while Mercedes-Benz doesn&#39;t sell any EVs at all in the US yet. </p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a Check with each winery for the latest details as you plan your visit. Many wineries are operating with reduced capacity, limited indoor seating, mask requirements (when not tasting wine), and enhanced cleaning measures. Some wineries are also requiring reservations and restricting the number of guests who can visit, so consult their websites and make reservations in advance if you can.&#160;</p><p>State and local COVID-19 restrictions will also impact how each winery is able to operate. <a href=\"https://www.napavalley.com/blog/visiting-napa-valley-during-covid-19/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Napa Valley</a>, for example, is advising visitors to wear masks and practice social distancing. In general, expect limited interaction between customers and servers at tasting rooms, contactless ordering and payment, and even temperature checks before entering some wineries.&#160;</p><h2>What's the best time to visit a winery?</h2><p>Keep in mind that vineyards are working farms, so they'll be busy places during peak grape harvest season (roughly July to October, depending on the region). A winery (where wine is produced) may be separate from the actual vineyard, and a tasting room might also be separate from the growing operation.</p><p>Many are open year-round, but check with the winery for specifics on their schedule, including any vineyard tours and wine-tasting programs they may offer. If you're hoping to have a chance to chat with a winemaker, you might want to choose a quieter time of year.&#160;</p><p>Keep in mind that finding available accommodation in high-demand areas during the peak summer and fall seasons can be a challenge, so book early to avoid disappointment.</p><h2>What are the best wine regions in the US?</h2><p>There are currently <a href=\"https://www.ttb.gov/wine/established-avas\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">252 established AVAs</a> across the country, reflecting a wide range of growing conditions and geographic features in states you might expect (California, Washington, Oregon, New York), and those which might surprise you (Texas, Arizona, New Jersey, Wisconsin). In fact, the oldest AVA is actually in Missouri (the Augusta AVA, established in 1980, just a few months before Napa Valley). There's a wine region for every taste, and that's what makes them so much fun to explore on your way to finding your own personal favorite.&#160;</p><p><a href=\"https://www.washingtonwine.org/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Washington State</a> has 16 AVAs producing over 70 grape varieties. The <a href=\"https://www.washingtonwine.org/wine/facts-and-stats/regions-and-avas/yakima-valley\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Yakima Valley AVA</a> is known for chardonnay, Riesling, merlot, cabernet sauvignon, and syrah.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.oregonwine.org/\">Oregon</a>'s 19 AVAs grow nearly 100 grape varieties. The Willamette Valley's <a href=\"https://eolaamityhills.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Eola-Amity Hills AVA</a> is known for its pinot noir and chardonnay; and the <a href=\"https://yamhillcarlton.org/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Yamhill-Carlton AVA</a> specializes in pinot noir, chardonnay, and pinot gris.</p><p><a href=\"https://discovercaliforniawines.com/meet-the-grapes/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">California</a> has a whopping 141 AVAs, with over 100 varieties of grapes growing throughout the state. In Napa Valley, the <a href=\"https://www.calistogawinegrowers.com/calistoga-ava/calistoga-ava-facts/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Calistoga AVA</a> is known for producing cabernet sauvignon, zinfandel, petite sirah, charbono, and syrah. The <a href=\"http://www.mtveederwines.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Mount Veeder AVA</a> specializes in cabernet sauvignon, chardonnay, malbec, merlot, and syrah; and the <a href=\"https://appellationsthelena.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">St. Helena AVA</a> is recognized for cabernet sauvignon, cabernet franc, merlot, syrah, zinfandel, and sauvignon blanc. You'll find plenty of zinfandel and sauvignon blanc in Sonoma County's <a href=\"https://www.drycreekvalley.org/dry-creek-valley/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Dry Creek Valley AVA</a>; and the <a href=\"https://pasowine.com/paso-robles/ava/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Paso Robles AVA</a> has built a reputation for cabernet sauvignon, merlot, zinfandel, syrah, and chardonnay.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.txwines.org/\">Texas</a> has eight AVAs. The <a href=\"https://www.wine-searcher.com/regions-fredericksburg+in+the+texas+hill+country\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Fredericksburg in the Texas Hill Country AVA</a> specializes in chardonnay, chenin blanc, merlot, and pinot noir.</p><p><a href=\"https://coloradowine.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Colorado</a> has two AVAs. The <a href=\"https://coloradowine.com/the-tradition/terroir/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Grand Valley AVA</a> is known for syrah, merlot, cabernet sauvignon, and chardonnay.</p><p><a href=\"https://newyorkwines.org/wineries/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">New York's wine producers</a> are classified within 11 AVAs. The <a href=\"https://newyorkwines.org/wineries/hudson-valley-wineries/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Hudson River Region AVA</a> specializes in pinot noir, cabernet franc, Riesling, and merlot. <a href=\"https://www.fingerlakeswinealliance.com/avas/seneca-lake-ava/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Seneca Lake AVA</a>, in the <a href=\"https://www.fingerlakeswinealliance.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Finger Lakes</a> region, is recognized for its Riesling, cabernet franc, chardonnay, pinot noir, and Gewurztraminer. <a href=\"https://liwines.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Long Island</a>'s North Fork AVA is especially known for its cabernet franc, merlot, and chardonnay.&#160;</p><p><a href=\"https://www.virginiawine.org/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Virginia</a> has eight AVAs. The <a href=\"https://www.wine-searcher.com/regions-monticello\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Monticello AVA</a> specializes in chardonnay, cabernet sauvignon, cabernet franc, and viognier.</p><h2>Are Airbnbs safe?</h2><p>As summer approaches and vaccines roll out, we're all eager to travel again. The CDC recently announced that&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/cdc-fully-vaccinated-travelers-can-now-travel-in-the-us-2021-4\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\" data-uri=\"303f476a077d8164f790a3cf23ec1cf6\">fully vaccinated people can safely travel in the US</a>.</p><p>Experts also consider private vacation homes like <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/are-airbnbs-safe-coronavirus\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\" data-uri=\"1e6ea0063f937a96dc22dade5b4c7c6e\">Airbnbs, one of the safer</a> choices, especially when&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/which-is-safer-airbnb-hotels-coronavirus\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\" data-uri=\"3aa44a069ccdebdc5c7e8b56165c0439\">compared to hotels</a>. This is because you are often booking an entire home protected from interaction with others.</p><p>Airbnb also announced rigorous new procedures including the&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnb-new-cleaning-protocol\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\" data-uri=\"18a34ac984b0eaae3b22940000d05d74\">Enhanced Cleaning Protocol</a>, which includes guidelines on personal protective equipment, disinfectants, and mandatory waiting periods between previous guests and cleanings.</p><p>However, there are still serious <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/is-travel-safe-coronavirus\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">risks to traveling during the COVID-19 pandemic</a>, and it's important to follow advice from leading health organizations such as the CDC and the WHO. Look into the latest local and state guidelines before planning your vacation, and take precautions including wearing a mask, washing your hands frequently, and maintaining social distancing.</p><h2>What is Airbnb's cancellation policy?</h2><p>Airbnb cancellation policies are set by each home's host, so check the individual listing for details. You can read a full breakdown of <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnbs-cancellation-policy\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Airbnb's cancellation policies here</a>.</p>\n\tMore great
