2021 15:24:16 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/5d1a39a2a17d6c083f4163c9?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"8aefa81733d46343ec268a08a024da8f","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn35@2020_1/2021/04/14/18-15-27-715_0a373346ff38ab57.webp","destWidth":1400,"destHeight":1050,"sourceBytes":231784,"destBytes":231784,"author":"insider@insider.com (Blake Stilwell)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5d1a38dfa17d6c08b50b3282?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn78@2020_1/2021/04/14/18-15-35-018_ac6a996859c97d28.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn1@2020_2/2021/04/14/18-15-35-145_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=mKlW6tHaHwg:3sM4KXOts2k:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn29@2020_1/2021/04/14/18-15-31-591_e97f9164fde4be89.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=mKlW6tHaHwg:3sM4KXOts2k:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn89@2020_2/2021/04/14/18-15-35-327_0b6e8f03453b5a37.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn29@2020_4/2021/04/14/18-15-29-996_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=mKlW6tHaHwg:3sM4KXOts2k:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn14@2020_2/2021/04/14/18-15-36-326_4717ef5465d174d4.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/mKlW6tHaHwg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn77@2020_4/2021/04/14/18-15-29-272_02d972df5b3c6938.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1618424108858},{"createdTime":"2021-04-15 02:15:08","updatedTime":"2021-04-15 02:15:08","title":"The real reason we still haven't cloned humans","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/ethics-of-human-cloning-scientific-progress-2020-7","description":"<div style=\"position:relative; overflow:hidden; padding-bottom:56.25%\">\n<iframe src=\"https://cdn.jwplayer.com/players/VJznL6Za-jZbcmOYf.html\" width=\"100%\" height=\"100%\" style=\"position:absolute;\" allow=\"fullscreen\"></iframe>\n</div><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>We&#39;ve technically been able to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/ap-scientists-successfully-clone-monkeys-are-humans-up-next-2018-1\">clone human beings</a> for almost a decade.</li>\n<li>So, why haven&#39;t we? The answer has way more to do with science than <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/embryonic-stem-cells-lead-to-human-cloning-2013-5\">morality</a>. </li>\n<li>Not only is cloning inefficient and dangerous, there&#39;s just not a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/can-you-clone-a-human-2016-7?IR=T\">good enough reason</a> to make a human this way. </li>\n<li>But making entire copies of people isn&#39;t the only way we can potentially use <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/afp-china-clone-factory-scientist-eyes-human-replication-2015-12\">cloning</a> to benefit humans.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p><em>Following is a transcript of the video.</em></p><p><strong>Narrator:</strong> We&#39;ve been able to clone human embryos for about seven years. But as far as we know, no one&#39;s actually cloned a whole person. Turns out, ethics aren&#39;t the only thing holding scientists back. Cloning isn&#39;t the sci-fi marvel we think it is. It can be dangerous, often ineffective, and, most of all, we just haven&#39;t thought of a good enough reason to do it. So, here&#39;s why you&#39;ll probably never have to fight your evil clone.</p><p>This is Dolly. Just kidding, that&#39;s a regular sheep. This is Dolly, the first mammal cloned successfully from an adult cell. She was born in 1996 after scientists figured out how to remove the DNA from the egg cell of a Scottish Blackface sheep and basically replace it with the DNA of a mammary cell from a Finn Dorset sheep. They gave it a little electric shock to fuse the cell and get it replicating, placed the cells in the uterus of another sheep, and boom, clone. This method, called reproductive cloning, could theoretically be used on humans. But this is a best-case scenario. It took 277 tries for the scientists to get one Dolly. Nowadays, cloning mammals generally has a success rate of about 10% to 20%. Better than one in 277, but still a majorly inefficient process.</p><p><strong>Jose Cibelli:</strong> Technically, it&#39;s not difficult to produce a clone embryo, but human cloning has other hurdles that need to be considered.</p><p><strong>Narrator:</strong> To even research human cloning, scientists would need to ethically collect a large amount of donated eggs and find enough surrogates to carry them. But even if they made it through that logistical nightmare, the biggest issue is this:</p><p><strong>Cibelli:</strong> They&#39;re gonna hurt the baby, or they&#39;re gonna hurt the person carrying the cloned fetus.</p><p><strong>Narrator:</strong> Across the board, scientists have found that some embryos expire before they&#39;re implanted. Others result in miscarriages. And those that make it to term often die soon after birth or end up with severe abnormalities. Simply, these are risks that are easier to take when it comes to experimenting with sheep than with people. But arguably the biggest reason we haven&#39;t cloned a human being? There&#39;s not a good enough reason to.</p><p>In pop culture, cloning is used to bring people back from the dead. But that&#39;s not how it works. Cloning someone would only create a twin, not a replica, since identical twins have the same genetics, but not necessarily personalities. And a &#34;Never Let Me Go&#34; scenario, where organs are harvested from clones to save the rich, is not only unethical, but unnecessary. Why clone an entire person when you can just make the part you need? Something, theoretically, therapeutic cloning can solve.</p><p>Therapeutic cloning is almost identical to reproductive, except the cloned embryo is never implanted in a uterus. Instead, the embryo is cloned for the sole purpose of extracting stem cells. Stem cells have the incredible ability to turn into any other cell in the human body, which means they&#39;re great for developing new treatments for disease and have the potential to repair or regenerate tissues and organs.</p><p>But, no surprise, there are a lot of downsides with therapeutic cloning. The thing about stem cells is that they&#39;re a pretty limited resource. The most substantial source for embryonic stem cells? Three- to five-day-old embryos, cloned or otherwise. And when someone else&#39;s stem cells are transplanted into a patient, the body will sometimes fight them off like a disease. Some researchers believe that cloned stem cells, since they share the patient&#39;s DNA, would be less likely to be rejected. But this use case is still in the research stage.</p><p>And, finally, therapeutic cloning is an individualized treatment in a world where drug companies are more interested in standardized ones. And there are easier ways to create multipurpose cells nowadays, like the method for creating induced pluripotent stem cells. They&#39;re basically adult cells that have been reprogrammed to be a different type of cell.</p><p><strong>Cibelli:</strong> The problem with therapeutic cloning, of course, is that you need a lab personnel that is qualified to do it, specific equipment to do it. Whereas the other technique, you can just buy a kit and one person can do it in a lab that has some expertise in tissue culture.</p><p><strong>Narrator:</strong> Cloned cells still have an advantage when it comes to healthier mitochondria and the ability to grow into entire animals, whereas iPSCs often peter out. But since iPSCs safely and reliably do most everything but create entire living animals, why fund the harder, ethically ambiguous thing? So, cloning might actually have a bigger place in movies than it does in real life, because the money just isn&#39;t there. And just because we can do something doesn&#39;t mean we need to.</p><p><strong>Ian:</strong> Your scientists were so preoccupied with whether or not they could, they didn&#39;t stop to think if they should.</p><p><strong>Abby Tang:</strong> So, in the research for this video, I did come across one very interesting tidbit, and that is the announcement of cloned human baby Eve, who was born on December 26, 2002. And the source of this announcement is a company called Clonaid, which was formed in 1997 by the Raelian cult. And they&#39;re a cult that believes that humans were cloned from aliens and the only way for us to reach immortality is to clone ourselves. It&#39;s been 18 years, and we haven&#39;t gotten any proof that baby Eve exists or has ever existed, but the company is still alive and well. So if any proof does come through, we will update you. </p><p><em>EDITOR&#39;S NOTE: This video was originally published in July 2020.</em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on 02:15:08","updatedTime":"2021-04-15 02:15:08","title":"Luxury items like watches and jewelry are getting even more expensive","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/price-of-luxury-items-watch-jewelry-increases-more-expensive-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f64d365323fc4001e0d71ab?format=jpeg\" alt=\"luxury jewelry covid\" height=\"1333\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.gettyimages.com/detail/news-photo/shop-manager-giulia-pietersen-checks-jewellery-items-at-an-news-photo/1213459615?adppopup=true\" target=\"_blank\">Miguel Medina/AFP via Getty Images</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The cost of goods in the US saw its largest monthly increase since 2012.</li>\n<li>Jewelry and watches were among several items that saw a significant price boost.</li>\n<li>Prices are expected to continue rising in the coming months as vaccination levels increase.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Luxury items became even more expensive last month as the price of goods in the US saw its highest monthly increase in nearly 9 years, according to the US Bureau and Labor Statistics&#39; <a href=\"https://www.bls.gov/news.release/cpi.t02.htm\">Consumer Price Index.</a></p><p>Jewelry and watches were among several items that pushed the overall surge in prices. The cost of jewelry in the US rose 7.4% from the previous year and nearly 6% between February and March, according to the index.</p><p>Similarly, the price of watches also rose 4.3% from 2020 and 2.4% in the past month alone. </p><p>While the price increase might not seem particularly high on a surface level, they could put a further strain on the wallets of people buying big-ticket items.</p><p>If applied to the average price of a Rolex in 2020 - which falls around $12,000, according to <a href=\"https://wristadvisor.com/how-much-is-a-rolex-and-what-is-a-rolex-worth/\">Wrist Advisor</a> - rising prices mean buyers can add about $500 to the price tag.</p><p>And that&#39;s just for the average buyer. Customers looking to purchase even more pricey watches, like Rolex&#39;s $75,000 model, would have to tack on an additional $3,000 to that price tag.</p><p>Similarly, for couples looking to buy a diamond engagement ring - an item with an average price around $5,000, according to <a href=\"http://www.jewelrywise.com/engagement-wedding/article/how-much-should-i-expect-to-pay-for-an-engagement-ring#:~:text=On%20average%2C%20according%20to%20jewelry,stones%20you%20choose%20to%20add.\">Jewelry Wise</a> - buyers can expect to pay an additional $370 this year, or even see a price increase of $285 from the previous month.</p><p>Prices in the US are only expected to continue to rise in the coming months, as increased vaccination rates allow the economy to reopen and demand to surge.</p><p>The cost of goods has also been impacted by several supply disruptions, including a shipping container shortage, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.in/thelife/news/the-us-has-its-own-supply-chain-crisis-brewing-as-dozens-of-cargo-ships-remain-stuck-off-the-coast-of-la-as-they-wait-to-dock/articleshow/81899636.cms\">port delays in California</a>, and the impact of the Texas freeze on production in the state. Many companies are also still struggling to meet demand after cutting back on production due to COVID-19 shutdowns last year.</p><p>Outside of watch and jewelry prices, the Consumer Price Index showed several other goods had significant price increases, in particular fuel and food. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/gas-prices-skyrocketing-in-us-expected-increase-further-summer-2021-4\">Gas prices jumped over 9% in the past month and drove the largest increase in the index.</a></p><p>Overall, prices rose over last year at their highest rate since 2018, beating analysts estimates. The index rose 0.6%, while analysts estimated a 0.5% increase, according to <a href=\"https://www.investing.com/economic-calendar/cpi-69\">Dow Jones estimates.</a></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read Kay)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5f64d365323fc4001e0d71ab?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn9@2020_5/2021/04/14/18-15-35-255_eae44117090c5ca8.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn1@2020_2/2021/04/14/18-15-35-145_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=1ZWm-bSuTic:tTpwVyzsfWY:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn57@2020_3/2021/04/14/18-15-35-724_466aadd8df6fbbe2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=1ZWm-bSuTic:tTpwVyzsfWY:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn93@2020_4/2021/04/14/18-15-29-591_70b7c9748596c23b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn29@2020_4/2021/04/14/18-15-29-996_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=1ZWm-bSuTic:tTpwVyzsfWY:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn73@2020_5/2021/04/14/18-15-32-001_c57e009f7bf206f9.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/1ZWm-bSuTic":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn21@2020_6/2021/04/14/18-15-33-094_8f2d1d96b7bf5ba5.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1618424108857},{"createdTime":"2021-04-15 02:15:08","updatedTime":"2021-04-15 02:15:08","title":"Golden Corral is expanding on its buffet model with drive-thrus, alcohol and curbside pickup","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/golden-corral-to-expand-buffet-model-with-drive-thrus-alcohol-2021-4","description":"<figure> \n <img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5dc1917e7eece52a2c0aa816?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Golden Corral 23\" height=\"1335\" width=\"1780\" charset=\"\"> \n  <figcaption> \n   <p class=\"copyright\">Hollis Johnson</p> \n  </figcaption> </img>\n</figure>\n<ul class=\"summary-list\"> \n <li>Golden Corral pivoted to curbside pickup and drive-thru concepts during the pandemic.</li> \n <li>Buffets were closed across the country to slow the spread of the coronavirus.</li> \n <li>The chain is investing in alcohol options to attract new customers.</li> \n <li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider's business page</a>.</li> \n</ul>\n<p>Buffet chain Golden Corral is reworking its core business model by adding drive-thrus and alcohol, CEO Lance Trenary told Insider.</p>\n<p>Off-premises orders made up less than 3% of all business before the coronavirus pandemic, and the team started thinking about what changes could make business more sustainable when it eventually reopened. To do that, Golden Corral looked at restaurants with multiple access points - curbside, drive-thru, and delivery were all alternative ways customers could buy food without dining inside.</p>\n<p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/chipotle-outlines-its-strategy-for-deploying-nuro-autonomous-vehicles-2021-4\" data-e2e-name=\"inline-read-more-link\">Chipotle's tech chief reveals how its investment in Nuro's self-driving vehicles could 'solve' restaurants' delivery problems, as Domino's rolls out the autonomous vehicles this week</a></em></p>\n<p>Golden Corral started testing its own drive-thrus \"out of necessity,\" but they look different from a McDonald's or Chick-fil-A drive-thru, because Golden Corral restaurants weren't built with drive-thrus in mind. Instead, the chain created two options, Trenary said. The first is similar to carhop service, he told Insider. Customers place orders at a drive-thru screen as they would at any restaurant, then are directed to a parking spot, with a target to deliver food in three minutes.</p>\n<figure> \n <img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6076fd264206150018175684?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Drive Thru Menu Board in Test\" height=\"1441\" width=\"1922\" charset=\"\"> \n  <figcaption> \n   <p class=\"copyright\">Golden Corral</p> \n  </figcaption> </img>\n</figure>\n<p>The other model might more accurately be described as curbside pickup, but Golden Corral calls it a \"virtual drive-thru.\" Customers pull into a parking spot with a QR code to scan, which pulls up a menu where they can then place an order and have food brought to the car. The chain has six active drive-thrus, with plans to open more in coming weeks.</p>\n<p>\"Our business model was virtually outlawed overnight\" Trenary told Insider. None of Golden Corral's nearly 500 locations were allowed to open dining rooms in the early days of the pandemic, and \"there were some dark days,\" he said. </p>\n<p>Fast food and fast-casual brands across the country have <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/starbucks-chick-fil-a-drive-thrus-ipads-and-video-technology-2021-3\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\" data-uri=\"4a5a47c10c41ef75d335bace97eb3daf\">optimized drive-thrus</a> over the last year as they became crucial in the age of COVID-19. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mcdonalds-chipotle-double-down-on-high-tech-drive-thrus-2019-10\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\" data-uri=\"cfd0d0af0d6ecf66b5163ed5e0f27e39\">Drive-thru orders</a> have grown across the fast-food industry since the pandemic <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/mcdonalds-drive-thru-improvements-and-new-packaging-2020-11#mcdonalds-introduced-a-packaging-refresh-across-the-chain-1\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"80\" data-uri=\"c80b008cd499be172fc3f0289aec6b7d\">closed many dining rooms</a>.</p>\n<p>Drive-thrus have been up <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/7-eleven-drive-thru-in-texas-slurpees-tacos-2021-3\">industry-wide</a> because they are perceived as a \"<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/starbucks-chick-fil-a-drive-thrus-ipads-and-video-technology-2021-3\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-uri=\"4a5a47c10c41ef75d335bace97eb3daf\">safe way to use the brand\"</a> Kalinowski Equity Research founder Mark Kalinowski told Insider. </p>\n<p>Even chains that aren't typically associated with drive-thrus are hopping on the trend. Drive-thrus have been a \"lifeline\" for Krispy Kreme, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/krispy-kreme-drive-thru-lifeline-during-covid-2021-3\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-uri=\"ddbcb16f813f0e63bedabf6251cb2878\">the chain's CMO told Insider</a>, and salad chain <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/sweetgreen-drive-thru-planned-for-colorado-in-2021-2020-12\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\" data-uri=\"dc53e2ed0c30b55c6f907a940df33dfd\">Sweetgreen</a> plans to open its first drive-thru this year.</p>\n<figure> \n <img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6076fe7874da0300181e197d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"GCJack\" height=\"1194\" width=\"1592\" charset=\"\"> \n  <figcaption> \n   <p class=\"copyright\">Golden Corral</p> \n  </figcaption> </img>\n</figure>\n<p>Golden Corral also embraced another pandemic-induced trend: <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/booze-to-go-permanent-restaurants-alcohol-industry-underage-drinking-2021-4\">alcohol</a>. The chain was initially resistant to add alcohol to its family-friendly image, <a href=\"https://www.restaurantbusinessonline.com/operations/golden-corral-tests-drive-thrus-la-carte-menu-frozen-margaritas\">Restaurant Business Online reported,</a> but as alcohol sales increases across the country Golden Corral came around. The chain partnered with Icee and Coca-Cola to sell frozen drinks like a Jack and Coke Icee.</p>\n<p>The pandemic \"forever changed how consumers think about dining out,\" Trenary told Insider. He thinks the changes made over the past year will attract new customers because of the convenience, while <a href=\"https://www.restaurantbusinessonline.com/operations/golden-corral-tests-drive-thrus-la-carte-menu-frozen-margaritas\">loyal</a> fans are already beginning to return.</p>\n<p><em>Do you have a story to share about a retail or restaurant chain? Email this reporter at <a href=\"mailto:mmeisenzahl@businessinsider.com\">mmeisenzahl@businessinsider.com</a>.</em></p>\n<p> </p>\n<div class=\"read-original\">\n Read the original article on \n <a +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/5dc1917e7eece52a2c0aa816?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"17ec1b7cd2efcafd50dc19d234af74c4","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn47@2020_2/2021/04/14/18-15-21-400_a129f840f186b301.webp","destWidth":1780,"destHeight":1335,"sourceBytes":150414,"destBytes":150414,"author":"mmeisenzahl@businessinsider.com (Mary Meisenzahl)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5dc1917e7eece52a2c0aa816?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn47@2020_2/2021/04/14/18-15-21-400_a129f840f186b301.webp","https://i.insider.com/6076fd264206150018175684?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn42@2020_4/2021/04/14/18-15-35-677_6434cd1f72ef0246.webp","https://i.insider.com/6076fe7874da0300181e197d?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn25@2020_3/2021/04/14/18-15-29-046_9fffa39626632b8c.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn1@2020_2/2021/04/14/18-15-35-145_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=O0YJjB0N-lk:oE757UhO_24:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn29@2020_2/2021/04/14/18-15-35-645_d4309e3edcb52954.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=O0YJjB0N-lk:oE757UhO_24:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn61@2020_3/2021/04/14/18-15-30-390_e99489dbdb99fda6.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn29@2020_4/2021/04/14/18-15-29-996_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=O0YJjB0N-lk:oE757UhO_24:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn61@2020_4/2021/04/14/18-15-35-056_6c1e16e100f28e04.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/O0YJjB0N-lk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn18@2020_3/2021/04/14/18-15-32-225_7ad9b90f2189da3e.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1618424108857},{"createdTime":"2021-04-15 02:15:08","updatedTime":"2021-04-15 02:15:08","title":"Amazon's small-team structure means new projects get greenlit quickly and it's one of the secrets to the company's success. Here's how it works.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/behemoth-amazon-rising-agile-teams-jeff-bezos-robin-gaster-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6062f1e6c9d73b00186e9179?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Jeff Bezos Amazon\" height=\"2976\" width=\"3967\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Amazon has sometimes been called the &#34;company of 100 CEOs,&#34; because there are so many possible pathways to greenlighting a project.\n<p class=\"copyright\">MANDEL NGAN/AFP via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Dr. Robin Gaster is the CEO of Incumetrics and a visiting scholar at George Washington University Institute for Public Policy.</li>\n<li>The following is an excerpt from his book, &#34;<a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Behemoth-Amazon-Rising-Power-Seduction-ebook/dp/B08P3HQFZX\">Behemoth - Amazon Rising: Power and Seduction in the Age of Amazon</a>.&#34;</li>\n<li>In it, he reveals how Amazon&#39;s structure allows for the quick formation of small, agile teams.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p><em>The following is a book excerpt.</em></p><p>Amazon is famously organized into small &#34;two-pizza&#34; (8 -10 person) teams. This directly adds flexibility and agility. Small teams can move quickly.</p><p>Amazon&#39;s two-pizza teams are agile, developed flexible inter-team structures, offer clarity or purpose, and are fast to innovate. They are also highly autonomous: the Prime Now team was able to launch its pilot on the iPhone first even though Amazon is generally an Android company. When the workload for a team becomes too big, Amazon may decide to break it into multiple smaller teams to keep their agility.</p><p>But teams mostly form because an employee sees an opportunity - a big one like Prime Now or one of the countless smaller ones. That employee is free to seek support and sponsorship inside or outside his own current team.  </p><p>How that happens at Amazon seems quite different from most companies, which have clearly defined chains of command. For an idea to be implemented, it must move up the chain of command to the point where management is senior enough to act. If a decision involves financial resources or legal issues, those accountants and lawyers will need to be consulted. And all the way along, there are endless opportunities for vetoes. Often, one veto kills the project. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60672ccfa7d803001963e704?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Behemoth Cover\" height=\"939\" width=\"618\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Behemoth: Amazon Rising.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Robin Gaster</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h2><strong>In contrast, Amazon offers &#34;multiple paths to yes,&#34; as Bezos puts it. </strong></h2><p>Individuals can go outside their team or even their division to find a team interested in an idea. Teams can find any number of senior managers to sponsor and support a project.</p><p>Amazon has sometimes been called the &#34;company of 100 CEOs,&#34; because there are so many possible pathways to greenlighting a project. It&#39;s not that Amazon makes innovation easy. It&#39;s never easy. But Amazon&#39;s structure is designed to get to yes.</p><p>Think of these proto-teams - ideas without even a team yet - as the seeds for 1,000 flowers that many eventually bloom. Amazon is diligent about fertilizing the soil and watering them with resources, in the sure knowledge that many - perhaps most - will fail.</p><p>These proto-teams - often even a single employee - are watered with enough resources to initially test whether there is something worth pursuing; that may be time off task to work on the idea, some hours or days from other team members, possibly other resources.</p><p>This period is pre-pilot. As described above, innovators start by working backwards to develop a clear vision of what the project is for, who it will serve, and why specifically customers will benefit. As it comes into focus, and more evidence is added that the project is worth pursuing, it may attract more resources from inside and outside the original team. That might include part-time help from other areas like logistics or human resources or advertising.</p><p>At this stage, the project is adding resources with dotted lines from existing structures. An HR person may be helping to acquire talent, but they remain within their existing HR team. Further information resources are easily available because of Amazon&#39;s previous decision to manage information flows via API; emerging teams can access information without needing permission.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60672de3a7d803001963e70d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Robin Gaster Headshot\" height=\"2400\" width=\"3200\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Robin Gaster.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Regis Lefebure</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>At some point, the project/team gets the greenlight to move into pilot production. That will require significantly more resources, and the creation of a more focused team. Neil Ackerman explains that when he was starting to build a team for his Small and Light Fulfillment project, he searched for the team members he would need through the internal Amazon directory, and reached out to them for &#34;many many meetings for coffee&#34; over weeks of effort. Of the seven people he eventually asked to join the new team, three accepted, and he hired four from outside. </p><h2>As the project becomes more successful, its place in the overall Amazon hierarchy becomes more settled. </h2><p>It is no longer a pilot on an experiment; it&#39;s now a service within existing services. So Ackerman&#39;s Small and Light project became embedded as a successful tool for addressing the needs of the Marketplace. Over time, it attracted further use from Amazon Retail, and it&#39;s now a permanent service within the Amazon logistics network, reporting up through that chain of command, and funded through the standard OP1 mechanism. As projects solidify, teams become fully independent entities within the Amazon ecosystem. They have their own marketing, sales, engineering, and finance functions, so each product has its own profit-and-loss statement, and thus each has both autonomy and accountability.</p><p>So what&#39;s different here, and what differences does it make?</p><p>The main difference is that Amazon&#39;s internal environment is set up to encourage the constant formation of teams, and provides the critical early resources that let them flourish quickly. Management expects and even demands innovation, and the structure is set up to provide enough fertilizer at the earliest stages, sufficient support during the prototyping and testing phase, and enough clear pathways to final adoption. There are far fewer vetoes, and more widely distributed resources and pathways. And that matters. As Benedict Evans observes,</p><p style=\"padding-left: 40px;\"><em>The structural advantage of them [teams], in Amazon at least (and in theory, at least) is that you can multiply them. You can add new product lines without adding new internal structure or direct reports, and you can add them without meetings and projects and process in the logistics and ecommerce platforms. You don&#39;t (in theory) need to fly to Seattle and schedule a bunch of meetings to get people to implement support for launching makeup in Italy, or persuade anyone to add things to their roadmap. This means not so much that products on Amazon are commodities (this is obvious) but that product categories on Amazon are commodities. </em>-Benedict Evans</p><p>Of course, this picture is somewhat idealized. Small teams also compete for resources and projects, so from another perspective Amazon has created a Darwinian environment in which teams compete vigorously (sometimes viciously) on behalf of their projects and initiatives. Not everything gets funded, so there are naturally winners and losers. This hyper-competitive environment is another way Amazon pushes teams to innovate. </p><p>One final note. Small teams are only possible because Amazon has, since its earliest days, required that all teams share information electronically not only with other Amazon teams, but with outsiders as well.  This key requirement makes it possible for hundreds of teams to connect - otherwise they would drown in information overhead, the sheer time and resource cost of communicating by manual methods like email and messaging. </p><p><em>Excerpt from <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Behemoth-Amazon-Rising-Power-Seduction-ebook/dp/B08P3HQFZX\">Behemoth - Amazon Rising: Power and Seduction in the Age of Amazon</a> reprinted with permission by Dr. Robin Gaster.</em></p><p><em>Dr. Robin Gaster is the CEO of Incumetrics and a visiting scholar at George Washington University Institute for Public Policy. He is the author of Behemoth - Amazon Rising: Power and Seduction in the Age of Amazon.</em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a market","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-market-outlook-clubhouse-retail-investing-indiviudal-shareholder-carparts-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/607703da74da0300181e19a1?format=jpeg\" alt=\"clubhouse app\" height=\"1000\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jakub Porzycki/NurPhoto via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Corporate execs are using audio-conferencing app Clubhouse to directly talk to retail investors. </li>\n<li>It&#39;s a move to recruit more individual stockholders after decades of mutual funds dominating portfolios. </li>\n<li>CarParts.com used Clubhouse to field questions from retail investors after its earnings report, per the Times.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\"></a><a href=\"https://newsletter.businessinsider.com/join/4np/10-things-opening-bell?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestce=markets&#38;utm_medium=ingest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Sign up here for our daily newsletter, 10 Things Before the Opening Bell.</a></li>\n</ul><p>Corporate executives are using audio-conferencing app Clubhouse to directly communicate with retail investors, according to reporting from the <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/04/13/business/stock-market-investors.html?campaign_id=4&emc=edit_dk_20210414&instance_id=29215&nl=dealbook&regi_id=61427258&segment_id=55546&te=1&user_id=6ce77f080f3d64e6312881475ed3b6767f080f3d64e6312881475ed3b676\">New York Times&#39; Matt Phillips</a>. <br><br>After hosting a post-earnings report conference call with Wall street analysts, executives at CarParts.com turned to Clubhouse to field questions from a group of over 2,000 listeners, the Times reported. Audience members asked questions like: How does the business work? Are CarParts.com shares worth buying? </p><p>It&#39;s a move that appears to be an effort to communicate more directly with retail investors and recruit more individual shareholders after decades of mutual funds dominating investor portfolios. </p><p>CarParts.com&#39;s chief financial officer and chief operating officer called the Clubhouse session an experiment.</p><p>&#34;We&#39;re trying to disrupt the way people fix their cars,&#34; he told the Times.&#34;Is there a way for us to disrupt how retail investors communicate with management?&#34;</p><p>Retail investing boomed in 2020 as people stuck inside their homes and fueled with extra stimulus cash turned to commission-free apps like Robinhood during the pandemic. The amount of individual stock ownership also grew to the highest level since 2014. According to the Federal Reserve, <a href=\"https://fred.stlouisfed.org/series/HNOCESQ027S\">American households bought roughly $211 billion in individual stocks</a> last year.</p><p>Whether that trend of individual stock ownership will continue could depend on the investor fanbase that companies build, and Clubhouse is one avenue executives are using to get closer to retail investors. </p><p>Though a recent note from JPMorgan&#39;s global markets strategy team says that US retail investors are rotating away from buying individual stocks and stock options and towards buying more traditional equity funds, as was the case before the pandemic. <br><br>During the first week of April, stock ETFs saw strong inflows of $18 billion, JPMorgan noted. Meanwhile, measures of call option buying that rose to a record high in January have begun to subside over the past two months, a sign that retail investors are less willing to invest in call options on individual stocks. Similarly, JPMorgan found that equity baskets containing stocks popular with US retail trading platforms have also slowed over the past two months. </p><p>JPMorgan noted that monitoring retail flows into equity funds will be an important metric for determining the state of the individual stockholder.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pieces-planet-theia-buried-in-earth-mantle-2021-4\">an ancient planet that hit Earth and sank into the mantle</a>.</li>\n<li>The growing <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/why-earths-magnetic-north-is-moving-2019-4\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\">&#34;dent&#34; in the magnetic field</a> can cause <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/weak-spot-magnetic-field-growing-could-harm-satellites-2020-8\">malfunctions in satellites</a> and spacecraft.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Earth&#39;s suit of geomagnetic armor has a chink, and it&#39;s growing.</p><p>A <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/earth-magnetic-field-weakening-satellite-problems-2020-5\">weak spot</a> in our planet&#39;s magnetic field, located above the southern Atlantic Ocean, has been increasing in size over the last two centuries, and it&#39;s starting to split in two.</p><p>For those of us on the ground, this isn&#39;t cause for concern: The protective field continues to shield the planet from deadly solar radiation. But the South Atlantic Anomaly, as it&#39;s appropriately named, does affect satellites and other spacecraft that pass through an area between South America and southern Africa. That&#39;s because higher quantities of charged solar particles seep through the field there, which can cause malfunctions in computers and circuitry.</p><p>The source of this growing &#34;dent,&#34; as <a href=\"https://www.nasa.gov/feature/nasa-researchers-track-slowly-splitting-dent-in-earth-s-magnetic-field\">NASA calls it</a>, is a bit of a mystery. But scientists expect it to keep expanding.</p><p>&#34;This thing is set to increase in size in the future,&#34; Julien Aubert, a geomagnetism expert from the Paris Institute of Earth Physics, told Insider.</p><p>Aubert thinks that the dent may have a connection to two gigantic blobs of dense rock buried 1,800 miles inside the Earth. Because of their makeup, the blobs disturb the liquid metal in the outer core that generates the magnetic field.</p><p>Both blobs are &#34;millions of times larger than Mount Everest in terms of volume,&#34; <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pieces-planet-theia-buried-in-earth-mantle-2021-4\">according to Qian Yuan</a>, a researcher studying geodynamics at Arizona State University.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.hou.usra.edu/meetings/lpsc2021/pdf/1980.pdf\">Yuan&#39;s team</a> thinks the blobs are otherworldly in origin: After an ancient, Mars-sized planet careened into Earth, it might have left these pieces behind.</p><h2>Chunks of a 4.5 billion-old-year planet inside Earth</h2><p>Nearly 2,000 miles below Earth&#39;s surface, swirling <a href=\"https://www.nationalgeographic.com/science/2019/02/magnetic-north-update-navigation-maps/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">iron in the planet&#39;s outer core</a> generates a magnetic field that stretches all the way from there to the space surrounding our planet. </p><p>That swirl is generated, in part, by a process in which hotter, lighter material from the core rises into the semi-solid mantle above. There, it swaps places with cooler, denser mantle material, which sinks into the core below. This is known as convection. </p><p>The problem is that something at the boundary between the core and mantle underneath southern Africa is wreaking havoc on that convection, thereby weakening the strength of the magnetic field above it.</p><p>It&#39;s plausible, Aubert said, that one of the blobs Yuan&#39;s team is investigating is to blame.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6062419ac9d73b00186e90c1?format=jpeg\" alt=\"theia\" height=\"2400\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>An artist&#39;s depiction of a possible collision between a proto-planet like Theia and the Earth.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theia_%28planet%29#/media/File:Artist%27s_concept_of_collision_at_HD_172555.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">NASA/JPL-Caltech/Wikimedia Commons</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Yuan&#39;s research posits that the blobs are remnants of an ancient planet called Theia, which struck Earth in its infancy 4.5 billion years ago. The collision helped create the moon.</p><p>Following that crash, the thinking goes, two parts of Theia may have sunk and gotten preserved in the deepest part of Earth&#39;s mantle.</p><p>The animation below, based on a <a href=\"https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/File:LLSVP.gif\">2016 analysis</a>, shows the location of these planetary fragments. </p><div class=\"insider-raw-embed\"><a title=\"Sanne.cottaar, CC BY-SA 4.0 <https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-sa/4.0>, via Wikimedia Commonsommons\" href=\"https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/File:LLSVP.gif\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/29/LLSVP.gif?format=jpeg\" alt=\"LLSVP\" height=\"\" width=\"512\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\"></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></a></div><p>Yuan said these blobs - their technical name is large low-shear-velocity provinces - are between 1.5 and 3.5% denser than the rest of Earth&#39;s mantle, and also hotter.</p><p>So when these chunks get involved in convection, they could screw with the regular flow. That, in turn, may lead the iron in the core under southern Africa to swirl in the opposite direction from iron in other parts of the core.</p><p>The orientation of Earth&#39;s magnetic field depends on the direction the iron inside is moving. To have a strong magnetic field, the entire thing has to be oriented the same way. So any areas that deviate from the usual pattern weaken the field&#39;s overall integrity. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3d9051cdf25a001e84e4ed?format=jpeg\" alt=\"magnetic field\" height=\"320\" width=\"1038\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A visualization of the Earth&#39;s magnetic field.\n<p class=\"copyright\">NASA Goddard Space Flight Center</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Still, it&#39;s possible these low-shear-velocity provinces aren&#39;t to blame for the field&#39;s weak spot at all.</p><p>&#34;Why doesn&#39;t the same weakness occur in the magnetic field above the Pacific, where the other province is?&#34; Christopher Finlay, a geophysicist at the Technical University of Denmark, told Insider. </p><h2>A &#39;hostile region&#39;</h2><p>A weaker field enables more charged particles from solar wind to reach satellites and other spacecraft in low-Earth orbit. That can cause problems with electronic systems, interrupt data collection, and lead expensive computer components to age prematurely.</p><p>In the 1970s, 1980s, and 1990s, satellite failures were frequent in the South Atlantic Anomaly, Aubert said.</p><p>Even today, the <a href=\"https://www.esa.int/Applications/Observing_the_Earth/Swarm/Swarm_probes_weakening_of_Earth_s_magnetic_field\">European Space Agency has found</a> that satellites flying through the region are &#34;more likely to experience technical malfunctions,&#34; like brief glitches that can disrupt communications. That&#39;s why it&#39;s common for satellite operators to <a href=\"https://phys.org/news/2020-08-nasa-track-slowly-dent-earth.html\">shut down non-essential components</a> as the objects pass through the area.</p><p>The Hubble Space Telescope, too, passes through the anomaly in 10 of its 15 orbits around Earth each day, spending nearly 15% of its time in this &#34;hostile region,&#34; <a href=\"https://image.gsfc.nasa.gov/poetry/ask/q525.html\">according to NASA</a>.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/50bf9b586bb3f7143200000a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"hubble telescope\" height=\"680\" width=\"1024\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>NASA&#39;s Hubble Space Telescope in orbit.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"http://www.flickr.com/photos/gsfc/4399423028/\" target=\"_blank\">NASA Goddard Photo and Video</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h2>The weak spot is getting weaker</h2><p>Researchers use a set of three satellites, collectively nicknamed Swarm, to keep tabs on the South Atlantic Anomaly.</p><p>Some studies suggest the region&#39;s total area has <a href=\"https://www.earth-prints.org/bitstream/2122/9857/1/ADS_Toward_a%20geomagnetic%20transition_nhess_2013.pdf\">quadrupled</a> in the last 200 years, and that it <a href=\"https://www.frontiersin.org/articles/10.3389/feart.2016.00040/full#B7\">continues to expand</a> year over year. The anomaly has also weakened by 8% since 1970.</p><p>In the last decade, Swarm also observed that the anomaly has split in half<a href=\"https://www.esa.int/Applications/Observing_the_Earth/Swarm/Swarm_probes_weakening_of_Earth_s_magnetic_field\"></a>: One area of magnetic weakness has developed over the ocean southwest of Africa, while another sits east of South America. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6074ca152cc1ef0018da159d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"SAA_2020\" height=\"430\" width=\"700\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The strength of Earth&#39;s magnetic field in 2020, as measured by the European Space Agency&#39;s SWARM satellites. In blue is the weaker area of the field.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Wikimedia Commons/Christopher Finlay et. al/2020</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>This is bad news, according to Finlay, because it means the hostile region for spacecraft is going to get bigger.</p><p>&#34;Satellites will have problems not only over South America but be impacted when they&#39;re coming over southern Africa as well,&#34; he said.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/magnetic-field-weak-spot-linked-pieces-planet-inside-earth-2021-4'>Business 02:15:08","updatedTime":"2021-04-15 02:15:08","title":"Walmart, Delta, and Coca-Cola refused to join hundreds of other companies in opposing restrictive voting laws - here's why","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/walmart-delta-coke-avoided-statement-against-georgia-voter-restriction-laws-2021-4","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/606230c167187800184ad26c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Georgia polling place\" height=\"1333\" width=\"1777\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A voter walks to the entrance during early voting for the Senate runoff election, at Ron Anderson Recreation Center, Thursday, Dec. 17, 2020, in Powder Springs, Ga. Todd Kirkland/AP\n<p class=\"copyright\">Todd Kirkland/AP</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Hundreds of companies signed a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-companies-oppose-voting-restriction-laws-who-signed-who-didnt-2021-4\">statement opposing restrictive voting laws Wednesday</a>.</li>\n<li> Some notable companies, including Walmart, Delta, and Coca-Cola, opted not to join.</li>\n<li>JPMorgan, which didn&#39;t sign, said it made its own statement supporting voting rights last month.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>While <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-companies-oppose-voting-restriction-laws-who-signed-who-didnt-2021-4\">hundreds of major companies signed a new letter</a> Wednesday opposing restrictive voting rules in the wake of <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/georgia-lawmakers-pass-sweeping-election-administration-bill-2021-3\">Georgia&#39;s election law</a>, some notable ones - including Walmart, Coca-Cola, JPMorgan, and Delta Air Lines - declined to join the effort.</p><p>The letter, which ran as a full-page ad in the Wednesday edition of The New York Times and Washington Post, opposed &#34;any discriminatory legislation&#34; that limited people&#39;s ability to vote. United Airlines, American Express, Facebook, Target, investor Warren Buffett, and others joined the effort.</p><p>Last month, a smaller group of <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/black-business-leaders-urge-companies-fight-republican-voting-laws-2021-4\">companies signed a letter with similar sentiment</a> organized by Black business leaders. </p><p>But, <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/04/14/business/dealbook/ceos-voting-rights.html\">the Times reported</a>, several companies declined to sign Wednesday&#39;s letter, including Georgia-based Coca-Cola, Delta, and Home Depot, as well as Walmart and JPMorgan Chase. </p><p>&#34;We publicly made our own strong statement last month about the critical importance of every citizen being able to exercise their fundamental right to vote,&#34; a spokesperson for JPMorgan said.</p><p>The bank&#39;s chief executive, Jamie Dimon, was one of the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/jp-morgan-chase-jamie-dimon-speaks-against-georgia-voting-law-2021-3\">first major business leaders to speak out</a> against the law, saying on CNN that he encourages workers to exercise their right to vote and opposes any efforts that would prevent them from doing so.</p><p>When asked about not signing onto Wednesday&#39;s statement, a spokesperson for Home Depot said: &#34;We&#39;ve decided that the most appropriate approach for us to take is to continue to underscore our belief that all elections should be accessible, fair and secure and support broad voter participation, and to continue to work to ensure our associates in Georgia and across the country have the information and resources to vote.&#34;</p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/ceos-responding-georgias-voting-laws-isnt-benevolence-its-economics-profit-2021-4\" data-e2e-name=\"inline-read-more-link\">Corporate America&#39;s response to Georgia&#39;s new voting laws isn&#39;t benevolence. It&#39;s about economics and profit, experts say.</a></em></p><p>Coca-Cola didn&#39;t respond to a request for comment. The beverage-maker <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/georgia-calls-to-boycott-coca-cola-after-georgia-voting-restrictions-2021-3\">faced consumer boycotts</a> last month for not doing enough to oppose the bill. It later said it wanted to be &#34;crystal clear&#34; that it was disappointed in the outcome of the Georgia voting law. That sparked former <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/photo-suggests-trump-still-drinking-coke-products-despite-calls-for-boycott-2021\">President Donald Trump,</a> a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/photo-suggests-trump-still-drinking-coke-products-despite-calls-for-boycott-2021\">noted Diet Coke fanatic</a>, to tell his followers to protest the company. </p><p>Delta and Walmart also didn&#39;t respond to Insider&#39;s request for comment.</p><p>Amid pressure to condemn the Georgia voting law, Delta CEO Ed Bastian blasted the legislation last month, saying it was &#34;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/delta-ceo-blasts-georgia-voting-rights-law-2021-3\">based on a lie</a>.&#34;</p><p>The Times reported that Walmart CEO Doug McMillon told employees in a note that the company is &#34;not in the business of partisan politics,&#34; noting that the retailer focuses on business issues such as taxes and regulation. In the note, he added that &#34;broad participation and trust in the election process&#34; are essential to the integrity of elections.</p><p>In March, Georgia Gov. Brian Kemp signed the election bill, known as <a href=\"https://www.documentcloud.org/documents/20527915-sb-202-as-passed\">SB202</a>, into law. The legislation made ballot drop boxes permanent, but only at select locations during limited hours, and shortened the window for requesting absentee ballots. The law also banned ballot selfies, and expanded early voting dates and hours in most counties, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/georgia-new-election-law-means-for-voters-and-officials-explainer-2021-3\">among other restrictive measures</a>.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the from Coinbase.</a></p><p>The surge higher helped push the dog-meme-cryptocurrency&#39;s total market value to as much as $18 billion, based on its current outstanding circulating supply of 129.2 billion dogecoin. </p><p>Besides <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/news/dogecoin-creator-sold-coins-years-ago-laid-off-cryptocurrency-mania-2021-2-1030077260\">being created as a joke,</a> Dogecoin is unique from other cryptocurrencies in that an unlimited amount of the coin can be mined, meaning the is limitless supply of dogecoin. Alternatively, bitcoin has a fixed supply of 21 million coins, of which nearly 19 million bitcoin have already been mined.</p><p>But some are buying into the dog-meme joke, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/news/dogecoin-price-surges-tweets-from-elon-musk-snoop-dogg-cryptocurrency-2021-2-1030055654\">including celebrities</a> like <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/elon-musk-dogecoin-tweets-bought-for-son-crypto-bitcoin-tesla-2021-2-1030067740\">Tesla CEO Elon Musk</a> and Guy Fieri of Diners, Drive-Ins, and Dives, who have both tweeted support for the Shiba-Inu inspired cryptocurrency.</p><p>&#34;Rollin&#39; out to the MOON [rocket emoji] #Dogecoin,&#34; <a href=\"https://twitter.com/GuyFieri/status/1382036182507343879\">Fieri tweeted on Tuesday</a>, accompanied with a picture of Fieri in an astronaut suit holding a space-suited up Dogecoin mascot.</p><p>Dogecoin isn&#39;t the only cryptocurrency that has surged to record highs this week. Amid <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/news/coinbase-ipo-predictions-expert-analysis-direct-listing-bitcoin-crypto-2021-4-1030290743\">growing anticipation of Coinbase&#39;s direct listing</a> later today, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/news/bitcoin-price-record-high-coinbase-direct-listing-btc-crypto-2021-4-1030302632\">bitcoin surged to record highs above the $64,000 level.</a> Ethereum also touched record highs on Wednesday, while litecoin, and XRP touched multi-year highs. </p><figure>\n\t<img 02:15:08","updatedTime":"2021-04-15 02:15:08","title":"10 ways to use the S Pen on a Samsung Galaxy device","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-use-s-pen-on-samsung-galaxy","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60768997420615001817556d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"samsung Galaxy Note 8 S Pen writing\" height=\"814\" width=\"1628\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>There&#39;s a number of handy ways to customize and use your S Pen on a Samsung Galaxy device.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Sarah Jacobs/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li aria-level=\"1\">To use the S Pen on a Samsung Galaxy device, you&#39;ll need to release it from its holder and tap the screen.</li>\n<li aria-level=\"1\">The S Pen stylus comes with all Galaxy Note devices, and some Galaxy and Galaxy Tab devices.</li>\n<li aria-level=\"1\">Beyond the traditional stylus actions, there are additional features that can make the S Pen even more useful. </li>\n<li aria-level=\"1\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tech-reference\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Visit Insider&#39;s Tech Reference library for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/s-pen\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">S Pen</a> is a stylus that&#39;s designed to work with the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/samsung-galaxy\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Samsung Galaxy</a>, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/galaxy-note\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Galaxy Note</a>, and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/category/galaxy-tab\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Galaxy Tab</a> phones and tablets. </p><p>If it came with your Galaxy device, you won&#39;t need to connect it, but there are still a few steps needed to use it. And the newer your device, the more features you&#39;ll have access to with the S Pen.</p><h2>How to use S Pen on Samsung Galaxy</h2><p>You can start using the <a href=\"https://www.anrdoezrs.net/links/6415797/type/dlg/https://www.samsung.com/us/mobile/mobile-accessories/phones/galaxy-note10-s-pen-blue-ej-pn970blegus/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow nofollow noopener sponsored sponsored\">S Pen</a> by pressing on the end of it to release it from your Galaxy device. Your Galaxy will vibrate to let you know that it recognizes you&#39;ve released it.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/607687ba4206150018175564?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Galaxy Note 5 S Pen Stylus\" height=\"795\" width=\"1590\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Press in the S Pen to release it from the holder.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Antonio Villas-Boas/Tech Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Your S Pen should start working immediately. If it doesn&#39;t, hover the S Pen over the screen and quickly double-press the button in the middle of the stylus.</p><h2>Ways to use the S Pen</h2><p>You can use the S Pen to do anything that you could normally do with your finger. And depending on the <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B08BX8BZ1P/ref=as_li_tl?ie=UTF8&tag=bitht_041221_how-to-use-s-pen-on-samsung-galaxy-20&camp=1789&creative=9325&linkCode=as2&creativeASIN=B08BX8BZ1P&linkId=c23a7c9828335d4f2e2bfdbdd1b796e528335d4f2e2bfdbdd1b796e5\" rel=\"nofollow sponsored\">Galaxy Note</a> or <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B08QQTQNDC/ref=as_li_tl?ie=UTF8&tag=bitht_041221_how-to-use-s-pen-on-samsung-galaxy-20&camp=1789&creative=9325&linkCode=as2&creativeASIN=B08QQTQNDC&linkId=7f898ce9b2de53ee4b47d97ee47f1be9b2de53ee4b47d97ee47f1be9\" rel=\"nofollow sponsored\">Tab</a> model you have, you may be able to use some or all of the following useful features. Test them all out and see which ones you like.</p><p><strong>Take notes on the lock screen.</strong> Simply take out your S Pen and write on the locked screen.</p><p><strong style=\"color: #222222;\">Customize the pen button.</strong> Press and hold the pen button. Go into your settings&#39; advanced features section for the S Pen and select &#34;S Pen remote&#34; or &#34;Air actions.&#34; Then tap &#34;Hold down Pen button to&#34; and select the desired option.</p><p><strong>Annotate a PDF.</strong> Open the desired PDF file in the Samsung Notes app and write your notes on it with the S Pen as you read.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60768ca3420615001817556f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"samsung galaxy s pen\" height=\"1371\" width=\"2742\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Write or draw on PDFs and images with your stylus.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Samsung</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong>Automatically change your handwriting to text.</strong> Turn on your <a href=\"https://www.anrdoezrs.net/links/6415797/type/dlg/https://www.samsung.com/us/mobile/mobile-accessories/phones/galaxy-note10-s-pen-blue-ej-pn970blegus/\" rel=\"nofollow sponsored\">S Pen</a> and open the Samsung Notes app. Create your handwritten note and hit save, then tap the handwriting-to-text icon in the lower toolbar. </p><p><strong>Turn your stylus into a remote.</strong> Go into your settings, then select &#34;Advanced Features,&#34; and then &#34;S Pen,&#34; followed by &#34;Air Actions.&#34; Then tap the toggle to turn on the &#34;S Pen remote&#34; option.</p><p><strong>Remotely take photos and videos.</strong> Follow the steps above to use the stylus as a remote. Then, when you have the camera open and ready, simply tap the end of the stylus once to take a photo or begin a video. Tapping twice will switch between the front and rear cameras. This works when the stylus is less than 10 meters away from the device.</p><p><strong>Control your music and other media with the <a href=\"https://www.anrdoezrs.net/links/6415797/type/dlg/https://www.samsung.com/us/mobile/mobile-accessories/phones/galaxy-note10-s-pen-blue-ej-pn970blegus/\" rel=\"nofollow sponsored\">S Pen</a>.</strong> Once you&#39;ve set up your S Pen as a remote, you&#39;ll also have the ability to start and stop your media by tapping the end of the stylus while watching a video or listening to music.</p><p><strong>Customize air actions.</strong> Swipe down on your device, and on the notification panel, select &#34;S Pen air actions.&#34; Under &#34;App actions,&#34; select the app you want to customize. Tap the item you want to customize and select either &#34;Pen button&#34; or &#34;Gestures.&#34;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60768c6974da0300181e1879?format=jpeg\" alt=\"samsung galaxy s pen\" height=\"800\" width=\"1200\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Air actions, also known as &#34;air commands,&#34; give you quick access to useful features.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Samsung</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong>Use direct pen input.</strong> This is turned on by default and allows you to write in text boxes, like in the Messages, Internet, or Phone app, and also converts your handwriting to text.</p><p><strong>Advance through a slide deck.</strong> Open a presentation on your phone, then pull down your notification menu and choose to use your phone as a touchpad. Go into presentation mode and click your pen once to go to the next slide, or twice to go back a slide.</p><bi-shortcode id=\"related-article-module-end-of-article\" class=\"mceNonEditable\"><a driving system to rival Tesla Autopilot on Wednesday.</li>\n<li>BlueCruise will enable hands-free driving on more than 100,000 miles of North American highways. </li>\n<li>It will be available for certain F-150 trucks and Mustang Mach-E crossovers later in 2021. </li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Ford has teased hands-free driving capability for a while, and on Wednesday revealed the first details about its system, including the name: BlueCruise.</p><p>The software will enable drivers to take their hands off the steering wheel and let the car do most of the work on more than 100,000 miles of North American highways, Ford said. Certain 2021 F-150 trucks and Mustang Mach-E crossovers can gain access to BlueCruise later in 2021 through an over-the-air software update. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/607707f074da0300181e19da?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Ford BlueCruise.\" height=\"1080\" width=\"1920\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Ford BlueCruise.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Ford</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>BlueCruise builds on Ford&#39;s existing driver-assistance suite, using radar sensors and cameras to keep a car in its lane, maintain a safe distance from other cars, and read speed limit signs. Drivers can switch on the system when they enter so-called &#34;Hands-Free Blue Zones,&#34; and the system lets drivers know when they&#39;re on a qualifying road through blue lighting on the instrument cluster. </p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/self-driving-stars-tips-for-getting-into-the-industry-2021-3\">How to break into the self-driving industry after college, according to 10 rising stars in the field</a></em></p><p>Like <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-autopilot-elon-musk-ford-porsche-bmw-2021-2?r=tl-sub\">Tesla&#39;s Autopilot</a> and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-tesla-autopilot-compares-to-cadillac-super-cruise-2017-10\">General Motors&#39; Super Cruise</a>, BlueCruise is an SAE Level 2 driver-assistance system that isn&#39;t fully autonomous and requires full driver attention. A driver-facing camera mounted above the steering wheel monitors a driver&#39;s head position and eyes to ensure they&#39;re paying attention to the road, similar to Super Cruise. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-in-car-cameras-pose-privacy-risk-consumer-reports-2021-3\">Tesla</a>, on the other hand, requires drivers to place a hand on the steering wheel rather than monitoring their gaze. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/607707ee42061500181756f0?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Ford BlueCruise.\" height=\"1334\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Ford BlueCruise.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Ford</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Tesla, despite facing mounting scrutiny over <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-touts-safeguards-as-senator-urges-company-to-rebrand-autopilot-2020-1\">Autopilot&#39;s branding</a> and its role in several <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/nhtsa-detroit-tesla-crash-michigan-autopilot-fsd-tractor-2021-3\">recent car crashes</a>, is one of the top companies to beat when it comes to driver-assist technology, and Ford acknowledges that. Ford on Wednesday said BlueCruise is &#34;similar to Tesla Autopilot but with the advantage of offering a true hands-free driving experience.&#34;</p><p>In a Wednesday <a href=\"https://twitter.com/jimfarley98/status/1382323413826555904\">tweet</a> announcing BlueCruise, Ford CEO Jim Farley took a dig at Tesla&#39;s &#34;Full Self-Driving&#34; software, a successor to Autopilot that the firm is <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-full-self-driving-beta-videos-show-flaws-wide-release-2021-3\">beta testing</a> using thousands of its own customers on public roads. </p><p>&#34;BlueCruise! We tested it in the real world, so our customers don&#39;t have to,&#34; Farley said. </p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">-Jim Farley  (@jimfarley98) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1382323413826555904?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">April 14, 2021</a></blockquote><script async=\"\" src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>Ford said its engineers have completed more than 500,000 miles of testing using BlueCruise, including 110,000 miles during a road trip that took 10 vehicles across 37 US states and five Canadian provinces. </p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/607707f074da0300181e19d9?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Ford BlueCruise.\" height=\"1667\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Ford BlueCruise.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Ford</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>BlueCruise comes standard on the Mustang Mach-E CA Route 1, Premium, and First Edition models. It&#39;s available as an option on the Select trim for buyers who spend $2,600 on a &#34;Comfort and Technology&#34; package along with $600 on a three-year subscription to the system.</p><p>For most F-150s, BlueCruise will cost $995 for the underlying tech package, along with the $600 software fee. </p><p>At some point down the line, Ford plans to add more advanced capabilities like automated lane changes. It also aims to regularly update the system with thousands of additional miles of compatible roads. </p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a adults are feeling increasingly comfortable socializing in public places, according to <a href=\"https://morningconsult.com/views-on-the-pandemic/\">recent polling from Morning Consult.</a></p><p>Morning Consult has tracked public sentiments about daily life amid the pandemic since March 2020. As of April 12, approximately 44% of American adults said they wouldn&#39;t mind congregating with friends in social settings - a 63% increase since the beginning of January when it was at just 27%.</p><p>The survey interviewed 2,200 people and includes a 2% overall margin of error in its results.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/6077049642061500181756c3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Morning consult socialization poll\" height=\"524\" width=\"1271\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Morning Consult</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Of all participants in <a href=\"https://morningconsult.com/return-to-socializing/\">Morning Consult&#39;s survey</a>, people born in <a href=\"https://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2019/01/17/where-millennials-end-and-generation-z-begins/\">Gen Z</a> (born between 1997 and 2012) and <a href=\"https://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2020/04/28/millennials-overtake-baby-boomers-as-americas-largest-generation/\">Gen X</a> (born between 1965 and 1980) said they felt the most comfortable socializing in public at 50% and 51% respectively.</p><p>Nearly <a href=\"https://covid.cdc.gov/covid-data-tracker/#vaccinations\">23% of the US population have been fully vaccinated</a> against COVID-19, and nearly 37% have received at least one dose, a rapidly growing proportion as more than <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/graphics/covid-vaccine-tracker-global-distribution/\">3 million Americans receive a dose of the vaccine each day</a>. The vaccination rate may decrease slightly in the coming days since <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-plans-pause-johnson-and-johnson-vaccine-rollout-blood-clots-report-2021-4\">authorities paused</a> the use of the one-shot Johnson &#38; Johnson vaccine on Tuesday to investigate after six people who got the shot - out of 7.2 million - developed blood clots.</p><p>The COVID-19 pandemic halted nearly all social events in the US, leading to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/edm-live-music-industry-coronavirus-impact-on-djs-2020-8\">closed restaurants</a>, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/teachers-central-to-covid-19-transmission-in-schools-cdc-2021-2\">shuttered schools</a>, and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/travel-industry-one-of-the-hardest-hit-by-pandemic-2020-7\">decreased travel.</a> Insider previously reported polling of the numerous ways that the ongoing pandemic has affected American decision-making during the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/insider-poll-biden-voters-take-more-covid-19-precautions-thanksgiving-2020-11\">holiday season</a>, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/insider-poll-how-covid-19-influences-presidential-race-biden-trump-2020-10\">presidential voting</a>, and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/insider-poll-biden-voters-take-more-covid-19-precautions-thanksgiving-2020-11\">more</a>.</p><p>Dr. Anthony Fauci, the director of the National Institute of Allergy and Infectious Diseases, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fauci-how-behavior-activities-changed-after-covid-19-vaccination-2021-4\">told Insider&#39;s Aylin Woodward</a> that he still plans on avoiding restaurants and travel despite being fully vaccinated. He said that if Americans avoid crowds for a little longer, then the country may avoid another surge in COVID-19 cases and deaths.</p><p>&#34;If we could just hold on for a while,&#34; Fauci said, Ryan/The Boston Globe/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Moderna said it hopes to provide COVID-19 vaccine booster shots in the US by the end of the year.</li>\n<li>Booster shots are designed to protect against coronavirus variants that cause COVID-19.</li>\n<li>The spread of variants and slow vaccine rollouts have led to a rise in cases globally.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>COVID-19 vaccinations aren&#39;t stopping anytime soon.</p><p>Moderna said on Wednesday that Americans could start getting booster shots later this year to protect against coronavirus variants.</p><p>&#34;It is likely that the countries that have already achieved high vaccine coverage are going to be ready to shift their focus to boosters in 2022 and possibly even starting at the end of this year,&#34; Corinne M. Le Goff, Moderna&#39;s chief commercial officer, said during a call with investors.</p><p>Le Goff said that countries like the US that quickly inoculate their populations could start getting booster shots soon, but because <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/graphics/covid-vaccine-tracker-global-distribution/\">just about 5% of the global population</a> has been vaccinated, most countries would continue giving residents the initial shots.</p><p>&#34;I hope this summer to get the vaccine authorized for a boost so that we can help people getting boosted before the fall, so that we all have a normal fall and not a fall and winter like we just saw in the last six months,&#34; Moderna CEO Stéphane Bancel said in an interview with Insider on Tuesday.</p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/gsk-vaccine-research-covid-departures-uncertain-future-2021-4\" data-e2e-name=\"inline-read-more-link\">GlaxoSmithKline stumbled with COVID-19 shots. Now it&#39;s facing an exodus of US talent and an uncertain future as the world&#39;s vaccine leader.</a></em></p><p>The US had administered more than 85 million doses of Moderna&#39;s two-dose COVID-19 vaccine as of mid-April. <a href=\"https://covid.cdc.gov/covid-data-tracker/#vaccinations\">Nearly half of American adults</a> have received at least one shot of a vaccine from Moderna, Pfizer, or Johnson &#38; Johnson, according to the Centers for Disease Control and Prevention.</p><p>Though the vaccines authorized for emergency use in many countries are highly effective, delays in rollouts and the spread of variants have led to an increase in COVID-19 cases globally. Many European countries have <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/europe-germany-italy-enter-third-wave-of-covid-19-pandemic-2021-3\">enforced shutdowns and curfews</a> in the &#34;third wave&#34; of the pandemic, and COVID-19 cases reached record highs in <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/world/2021/apr/11/india-steps-up-vaccine-effort-as-covid-cases-hit-record-high\">India</a> and <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/us-health-coronavirus-brazil-numbers/brazil-has-record-coronavirus-cases-second-highest-24-hour-deaths-idUSKBN2BB2H6\">Brazil</a> this spring.</p><p>Epidemiologists have predicted that <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/when-will-the-pandemic-end-depends-on-coronavirus-variants-vaccines-2021-2\">COVID-19 will become endemic</a>, likely to continue spreading as a mild, flu-like illness after the pandemic subsides. Researchers may regularly produce booster shots to protect against new variants, similar to how they develop vaccines for the flu every season.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original 02:15:08","updatedTime":"2021-04-15 02:15:08","title":"How to insert a blank page in Word and keep your document's formatting intact","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-add-a-page-in-word","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60772ccb42061500181757d9?format=jpeg\" alt=\"woman typing on laptop\" height=\"1060\" width=\"2120\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>You can add a blank page or a page break in Microsoft Word.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Westend61/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>You can add a blank page into a Word document by clicking the Blank Page option in the Insert menu.</li>\n<li>Using this option will keep your Word document&#39;s formatting intact.</li>\n<li>You can also insert a new page break in a Microsoft Word document to add space between sections.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tech-reference\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Visit Insider&#39;s Tech Reference library for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Microsoft Word allows you to insert blank pages between existing pages with just a few clicks.</p><p>It&#39;s a helpful feature when you&#39;re working on long documents or presentations, because it seamlessly inserts a blank page without disrupting the format of the existing content.</p><p>Page breaks are another option for adding space between sections. This formatting tool moves the content after a page break to the beginning of the next page.</p><aside class=\"quick-tip headline-regular\"><p><strong>Quick tip:</strong> When you&#39;re working on a long, complex document, you can quickly add or look for blank pages and page breaks by clicking &#34;View,&#34; then selecting the &#34;Navigation Pane&#34; box, then &#34;Pages.&#34;</p></aside><p>If you want to add or insert a new blank page into your existing Word document, here are two ways to do it. </p><aside class=\"breakout-box headline-regular\"><h2><strong>How to add a page in Word </strong></h2><ol><li>To insert a blank page into your document, place your cursor near the word or line you want a new page. For example, if you want a new page between the second and third page of your document, place the cursor on the last typed line of page two.</li><li>Click Insert. </li><li><p>Choose Blank Page and wait for a new blank page to open.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60762a9c420615001817553f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Add Blank Page\" height=\"519\" width=\"857\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Place your cursor where you want the new page to be added and click Blank Page.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Abigail Abesamis Demarest/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></li></ol></aside><aside class=\"breakout-box headline-regular\"><h2><strong>How to add a page break in Word</strong></h2><ol><li>To insert a page break into your document, click to place your cursor near where you want the page break to begin. </li><li>Click Insert.</li><li><p>Choose Page Break.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60762ad94206150018175540?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Add Page Break\" height=\"509\" width=\"857\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Select Page Break to create a new page and move content with it.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Abigail Abesamis Demarest/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></li></ol></aside><aside class=\"quick-tip headline-regular\"><p><strong>Quick tip:</strong> If your Word document window is minimized and doesn&#39;t cover your entire screen, you may need to click a Pages option before selecting either Blank Page or Page Break. </p></aside><bi-shortcode
